## 1. Background information on the procedure

## 1.1. Type II variation

Pursuant to Article 16 of Commission Regulation (EC) No 1234/2008, Gilead Sciences Ireland Unlimited Company submitted to the European Medicines Agency on 11 November 2025 an application for a variation.

The following changes were proposed:

| Variation(s) requested   | Variation(s) requested                                                              | Type              |
|--------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------|
| C.I.6.a                  | C.I.6.a Addition of a new therapeutic indication or modification of an approved one | Variation type II |

Extension of indication for treatment of adult patients with PD-L1-negative metastatic triple- negative breast cancer or PD-L1-positive metastatic triple-negative breast cancer previously treated with an anti-PD-(L)1 agent in the curative setting for Trodelvy, based on results from study GS-US-592-6238 (ASCENT-03), which is a phase 3 study of sacituzumab govitecan (IMMU-132) versus treatment of physician's choice (TPC) in Patients With Previously Untreated, Locally Advanced, Inoperable or Metastatic Triple-Negative Breast Cancer Whose Tumors Do Not Express PD-L1 or in Patients Previously Treated With Anti-PD-(L)1 Agents in the Early Setting Whose Tumors Do Express PD-L1. As a consequence, sections 4.1, 4.4, 4.5, 4.8, 5.1 and 5.2 of the SmPC are updated. The Package Leaflet is updated in accordance. Version 4.1 of the RMP has also been submitted.

## Information on paediatric requirements

Pursuant to Article 8 of Regulation (EC) No 1901/2006, the application included an EMA Decision P/0018/2020 on the granting of a product-specific waiver.

## Information relating to orphan market exclusivity

## Similarity

Pursuant to Article 8 of Regulation (EC) No. 141/2000 and Article 3 of Commission Regulation (EC) No 847/2000, the MAH did not submit a critical report addressing the possible similarity with authorised orphan medicinal products because there is no authorised orphan medicinal product for a condition related to the proposed indication.

## Scientific advice

The MAH received Scientific Advice from the CHMP on 11 November 2021 (EMA/SA/0000069358). The Scientific Advice pertained to clinical aspects of the dossier.

## 2. Scientific discussion

## 2.1. Introduction

## 2.1.1. Problem statement

The scope of this variation is to add a new therapeutic indication for Trodelvy for the treatment of adult patients with unresectable locally advanced or metastatic triple-negative breast cancer (TNBC) based on the results of the ASCENT-03 (GS-US-592-6238) study.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Disease or condition

The MAH initially applied for the following indication:

'Trodelvy is indicated as monotherapy for the treatment of adult patients with unresectable locally advanced or metastatic triple-negative breast cancer (TNBC) who have not received prior systemic therapy for metastatic disease and who are not candidates for PD-1 or PD-L1 inhibitor therapy (see section 5.1).'

## Epidemiology and risk factors

Breast cancer is the most commonly diagnosed cancer and leading cause of cancer death in women globally as of 2022. 2.3 million women globally were diagnosed with breast cancer and 670,000 died from the disease in 2022 1 . Triple negative breast cancer (TNBC) accounts for approximately 15% of invasive breast cancers 2 .TNBC is more common in younger women than in older women and in black persons than in persons of other races and ethnic groups. Other risk factors for the disease include the presence of a breast cancer susceptibility gene (BRCA) mutation, premenopausal status, obesity, and maternal-related factors such as parity and age at first pregnancy (Trivers et al. 2009; Plasilova et al. 2016).

## Biologic features

TNBC is defined by a lack of oestrogen receptor, progesterone receptor, and HER2 expression in tumour cells.

## Clinical presentation, and stage/prognosis

Compared with hormone receptor-positive and HER2 positive tumours, TNBC is characterized by a more aggressive tumour biology and shorter overall survival with a low 5-year survival rate of approximately 12% 3 .

Historically, the majority of patients with TNBC experience disease recurrence, with studies reporting 25% of patients with metastatic TNBC presenting with de novo metastatic disease 456 ; however, with recent advances in the curative setting, such as treatment with intensive neoadjuvant and adjuvant chemotherapy, anti PD-1 or anti PD-L1 therapy, and PARP inhibitors, more contemporary data suggest a shift to 33% of patients with metastatic TNBC presenting with de novo metastatic disease 7 . TNBC is most commonly associated with visceral metastases affecting the liver, lung, and brain 8 .

## Management

Current standard treatment for recurrent/metastatic TNBC varies by subtypes. For patients with de novo metastatic TNBC or recurrence of &gt;6-12 months after the end of (neo)adjuvant immune

3  American Cancer Society. Triple-negative Breast Cancer. Available at: https://www.cancer.org/cancer/types/breastcancer/about/types-of-breast-cancer/triple-negative.html. Last Updated: 01 March.  2023

8  O'Reilly D et al. Overview of recent advances in metastatic triple negative breast cancer. World J Clin Oncol 2021

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

checkpoint inhibitors (ICI) most recent ESMO guidance recommends a combination of chemotherapy with an ICI for PD-L1 positive patients. PD-L1 negative patients with germline BRCA 1/2 mutations should be treated with a PARP inhibitor and gBRCA-wt PD-L1 negative patients should receive chemotherapy (ESMO living guideline 9 ).

Figure 1 De novo MBC or recurrence &gt; 6-12 months after the end of (neo)adjuvant ICI

<!-- image -->

- (a) ESCAT scores apply to genomic alterations only
- (b) Pembrolizumab may be considered as monotherapy in further lines in case of high PD-L1 positivity and no previous exposure to ICI
- (c) ChT physician's choice of nab-paclitaxel, paclitaxel or gemcitabine-carboplatin
- (d) Disease free interval should be ≥ 12 months in countries where this indication is approved (EMA approved, not

- (e) If not used previously
- (f) Preferred if imminent organ failure [V, B]
- ChT, chemotherapy; EMA, European Medicines Agency; ESCAT, ESMO Scale for Clinical Actionability of molecular Targets; FDA, Food and Drug Administration; ICI, immune checkpoint inhibitor; MCBS, ESMO-Magnitude of Clinical Benefit Scale; mTNBC, metastatic triple-negative breast cancer; mut, mutation; PARP, poly (ADP-ribose) polymerase; PD-L1, programmed death-ligand 1; wt, wild-type .

The subset of patients with PD L1 positive metastatic TNBC (CPS ≥ 10) accounts for approximately 40% of patients with metastatic TNBC (Cortes et al. 2020). The prevalence of germline BRCA mutations is only 2% to 4% among patients with metastatic breast cancer and 9.3% to 15.4% among patients with TNBC (Armstrong et al. 2019). For the majority of patients, first-line treatment remains chemotherapy which is associated with a short median progression free survival (PFS) of 5.6 months and median overall survival (OS) of 16 months (Cortes et al. 2022). Therefore, there is still a significant unmet need for treatments for the subgroup of patients with TNBC who are not candidates for ICI (or PARPi).

## 2.1.2. About the product

Sacituzumab govitecan is an antibody-drug conjugate (ADC) composed of the following 3 components:

9  ESMO Living Guideline for Triple-negative metastatic breast cancer; G Curigliano et al., Ann Oncol. 2025.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

- The humanized monoclonal antibody hRS7 IgG1κ, which binds to trophoblast cell -surface antigen 2 (Trop-2), a transmembrane calcium signal transducer that is overexpressed in many epithelial cancers.
- The camptothecin-derived agent SN-38, a topoisomerase I inhibitor.
- A hydrolyzable linker, with the company designation as CL2A that links the humanized monoclonal antibody to SN-38.

Binding of Trop 2 by the parental RS7 antibody has been shown to result in internalization and processing of the antibody by the targeted cells. Because of its hydrolyzable linker, sacituzumab govitecan (SG) will release its SN-38 payload both intra- and extracellularly in the tumor microenvironment. SG delivers significantly greater amounts of SN-38 to a Trop 2-expressing tumour than conventional irinotecan chemotherapy. The extracellular release of SN-38 from SG also allows for bystander killing of Trop 2 negative tumour cells. Thus, SG can deliver cytotoxic chemotherapy to tumours, including adjacent cancer cells, in concentrations that are higher than those with standard chemotherapy and may reduce toxic effects in normal tissues that do not express the target.

Sacituzumab govitecan is approved in the EU for the treatment of adult patients with unresectable or metastatic triple-negative breast cancer (mTNBC) who have received two or more prior systemic therapies, including at least one of them for advanced disease (EC decision November 2021) and for the treatment of adult patients with unresectable or metastatic hormone receptor (HR)-positive, HER2negative breast cancer who have received endocrine-based therapy, and at least two additional systemic therapies in the advanced setting (Trodelvy EMEA/H/C/005182/II/0020, EC decision July 2023).

## 2.1.3. The development programme/compliance with CHMP guidance/scientific advice

## Scientific advice

The clinical efficacy and safety of SG for the treatment of adult participants with previously untreated locally advanced unresectable or metastatic TNBC have been evaluated in study GS-US-592-6238 (ASCENT-03). EMA scientific advice regarding the design of the phase 3 study was obtained in November 2021 (EMA/SA/0000069358). The MAH overall followed the CHMP's recommendations.

Related to eligibility criteria, CHMP was critical of the fact that gBRCA1/2 testing was not mandatory and recommended that patients with BRCA mutation should have received prior PARP inhibitor or alternatively, be excluded. -&gt; This recommendation was not implemented by the MAH.

CHMP further discussed that PD-L1 positive patients might be potentially eligible to ICI retreatment after (neo)adjuvant ICI treatment depending on the disease-free interval; therefore, the rationale for SG or TPC administration instead of using ICI-containing regimen for all patients with prior (neo)adjuvant ICI was not considered justified. -&gt; This was not considered relevant in view of recruited PD-L1 negative patient population (see below).

The proposed comparator and the proposed dosing regimens were considered overall acceptable, but possible differences in baseline characteristics and prognosis between the patients who will receive carboplatin/gemcitabine doublet or taxane could not be excluded and the MAH was encouraged to consider stratification according to TPC. -&gt; No stratification was implemented but prespecified subgroup analyses by TPC were implemented.

The optional crossover from the control arm at confirmed progression to SG was considered acceptable, since it would mirror the recommended treatment pathway and would likely occur also

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

outside the study, at least for patients who have received chemotherapy also in the (neo)adjuvant setting. The collection of data on sequencing of treatment, information on post-study treatment in both arms, as well as analysis of PFS2 was recommended. -&gt; PFS2 data were provided by the MAH during the ongoing assessment.

## 2.1.4. General comments on compliance with GCP

The assessment of the dossier has not raised concerns regarding GCP compliance of the pivotal study ASCENT-03.

## 2.2. Non-clinical aspects

No new clinical data have been submitted in this application, which was considered acceptable by the CHMP.

## 2.2.1. Ecotoxicity/environmental risk assessment

The environmental risk assessment (ERA) was previously submitted for Trodelvy® as part of the EU initial MAA. The EMA guideline on the Environmental Risk Assessment (ERA) states that 'the evaluation of the environmental impact should be made if there is an increase in the environmental exposure, e.g. a new indication may result in a significant increase in the extent of the use.' Given the dosing regimen will not change for the extension of indication and that the calculation is thus independent of the indication, an update of the ERA was not deemed warranted by the MAH and hence was not be submitted in the context of this extension of indication variation as the planned indication extension is within the environmental exposure predicted by the prior ERA. This is considered acceptable.

The Clinical trials were performed in accordance with GCP as claimed by the MAH.

The MAH has provided a statement to the effect that clinical trials conducted outside the community were carried out in accordance with the ethical standards of Directive 2001/20/EC.

## 2.3.2. Pharmacokinetics

With this application for extension of indication, the MAH is seeking approval of sacituzumab govitecan (SG, Trodelvy), a trophoblast cell-surface antigen-2 (Trop-2)-directed ADC, for locally advanced unresectable or metastatic triple-negative breast cancer (TNBC) patients who have not received previous systemic therapy for advanced disease and who were not candidates for programmed cell death protein 1 (PD-1) or programmed cell death ligand 1 (PD-L1) inhibitors.

The recommended dose of SG is 10 mg/kg administered intravenously (IV) once weekly on Days 1 and 8 of continuous 21-day treatment cycles until disease progression or unacceptable toxicity and thus is equal to the approved posology.

PK, and immunogenicity of SG were evaluated based on data from study GS-US-592-6238 and from 3 additional completed studies: Study IMMU-132-01, Study IMMU-132-05, and Study IMMU-132-09, whereas ongoing Study IMMU-132-06 contributed data to the immunogenicity package.

The PK of total antibody, free SN 38, and conjugated SN-38 was characterized in participants with solid tumors using an integrated PopPK model. The integrated PopPK model was also used to evaluate the effect of various intrinsic and extrinsic factors on the exposure of total antibody, SG, and free SN-38. Data from Studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU 132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238 were used to develop the model.

Pharmacokinetics of SG have been characterized throughout the initial marketing authorization procedure. In this variation assessment report, only summarized data on sacituzumab govitecan ADME, dose proportionality, special populations and interaction studies are presented.

In the pivotal Study GS-US-592-6238, serum samples for PK analyses were collected only for participants receiving SG. Collection times for PK samples were predose and after the end of infusion on Day 1 and Day 8 of Cycle 1; Day 8 of Cycles 2, 6, and 10. Thereafter, predose samples were collected on Day 8 of every 8 cycles after Cycle 10 (e.g. Cycle 18 Day 8, Cycle 26 Day8); and at the end of treatment (EOT) visit.

## Analytical methods

## Bioanalytical methods

Bioanalytical methods for the quantitation of total SN-38, free SN-38, SN-38G, and total antibody (hRS7-IgG and HRS7-SN38) in human serum were developed and fully validated at KCAS, LLC [Shawnee, Kansas, USA]) and then transferred and validated at Novotech Laboratory Services (formerly PPC-China Clinical Research Co., Ltd; Shanghai, China).

According to the MAH, all bioanalytical method validations, cross-validation between laboratories, and sample analysis reports supporting clinical studies were conducted according to the United States (US) Food and Drug Administration Bioanalytical Method Guidelines (2018) (U. S. Department of Health &amp; Human Services (DHHS) 2018), International Council for Harmonisation (ICH)-M10 Bioanalytical Method Validation and Study Sample Analysis Guidance for Industry (2022) (International Council for Harmonisation (ICH) 2022, U.S. Department of Health and Human Services (DHHS) 2022), and European Medicines Agency Guidelines on Bioanalytical Method Validation (2011) (European Medicines Agency (EMA) 2011).

The submitted bioanalytical methods for determination of total SN-38, free SN-38 and SN-38G, and total antibody (hRS7-IgG and HRS7-SN38) validated at KCAS Bio were already assessed during previous procedures and found to be adequately validated and overall acceptable for their intended purpose. Therefore, these methods are not listed and assessed in this report.

However, for the method validation VIMME1701E1 A3 (total SN-38) an Amendment No3 has been submitted, which included further long-term stability results (up to 1982 days at -80°C) and the evaluation of co-medication effects (domvanalimab, zimberelimab, and etrumadenant with its two metabolites A0304481 and A0003642) on the LC-MS/MS method for determination of free SN-38 and SN-38G. The pre-defined acceptance criteria and acceptance criteria of the ICH M10 on bioanalytical method validation (EMA/CHMP/ICH/172948/2019) were met. The updated results are considered acceptable.

The  assessment  of  the  partially-  (validation  report:  V1102206E1),  transferred-  (validation  reports: VR0327001-ENv01-A1, VR0333001-ENv01-A1, and VR0326001-ENv01-A2) and cross-validated bioanalytical methods, which were newly submitted with this application, is described below.

## Validation results

## · Method V11022061E1 for free SN-38

The bioanalytical method TP-80150 was partially validated at KCAS Bio (Olathe, Kansas, USA) under KCAS Project Number V1102206E1 and was performed for the determination of free SN-38 in human serum. KCAS method TP-80150 is an LC-MS/MS method identical to KCAS method TP70467 with the exception of SN-38G being removed from the preparations and analysis. Thus, the purpose of this partial validation was to remove SN-38 glucuronide from the existing test procedure showing that free SN-38 analysis is equivalent without SN-38 glucuronide. The assay was analyzed in the range of 1.00 500 ng/mL and is for use on human serum samples obtained during clinical trials.

The cross validation consists of evaluation of the following parameters:

## 1. Accuracy and Precision for SN-38 only

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

2. Cross validation of TP70467 with TP-80150. Analysis of pooled subject samples from clinical study will be run using both test procedures. Results were compared for cross validation. A total of 84 samples with reportable SN-38 concentrations were chosen to create a pool of 21 samples.

## · Method validation report VR0327001-Env01-A1 for total SN-38

The bioanalytical method AM0327001-ENv01 was validated at Novotech Laboratory Services (Shanghai, China) under Novotech validation report VR0327001-ENv01. Novotech method AM0327001-ENv01 is an LC-MS/MS method, and total SN-38 is defined as the combined amounts of free SN-38 in solution (unbound to the ADC [hRS7-SN-38]) and acid-dissociated (hydrolyzed) SN-38. Following hydrolysis, total SN-38 is extracted from human serum by protein precipitation and is quantified by reverse-phase HPLC-MS/MS with SN-38-d3 as an internal standard.

## · Method validation report VR0333001-ENv01-A1 for free SN-38 and SN-38G

The bioanalytical method AM0333001-ENv01 was validated at Novotech Laboratory Services (Shanghai, China) under Novotech validation report VR0333001-ENv01. Novotech method AM0333001-ENv01 is an LC-MS/MS method, where free SN-38 and SN-38G (i.e. both unconjugated to the SG antibody) are extracted from human serum by solid-phase extraction under yellow light and are quantified by reverse-phase HPLC-MS/MS, using SN-38-d3 and SN-38G-13C6 as internal standards.

## · Method VR0326001-Env01-A2 for total antibody

The bioanalytical method AM0326001-ENv01 was validated at Novotech Laboratory Services (Shanghai, China) under Novotech validation report VR0326001-ENv01 for the determination of SG total antibody (hRS7 unconjugated or conjugated with SN-38) in human serum. Novotech method AM0326001-ENv01 is an electrochemiluminescence (ECL) immunoassay that captures SG total antibody with anti-hRS7-IgG monoclonal antibody (mAb), and the complex is detected using a biotinylated anti-human IgG-Fc antibody followed by Sulfo-TAG Streptavidin.

## Laboratory Cross-Validation results of KCAS, LLC [Shawnee, Kansas, USA]) and Novotech Laboratory Services

Cross-validation of bioanalytical methods for the determination of total SN-38, free SN-38 and SN38G, and total antibody using spiked blank matrix and pooled clinical samples was conducted at KCAS Bio and Novotech to establish interlaboratory comparability.

The percentage difference of the mean cross-validation QCs (excluding low QC of Total SN-38) and the pooled clinical study samples (for total SN-38 and total antibody (hRS7 SN38 and hRS7-IgG)) met the pre-defined acceptance criteria. For free SN-38, no pooled clinical study samples were tested due to the limited freeze/thaw stability data for free SN-38. However, the assessment of bias (e.g. by Bland Altman plots or Deming regression) was not presented.

## ADA assay

Immunogenicity of SG or its components was assessed in clinical studies by evaluating and characterizing antidrug antibody (ADA) response using a semiquantitative electrochemiluminescence (ECL) immunoassay format to detect anti-SG antibodies and a multitiered approach that includes domain specificity testing. A competitive ligand-based ECL neutralizing antibody (NAb) assay method was developed and validated to evaluate the ability of ADAs to interfere with the activity of SG or its components.

These assay methods to detect the presence of ADAs and Nabs were developed and validated in accordance with agency guidance (European Medicines Agency (EMA) 2017, U.S. Department of Health &amp; Human Services (DHHS) 2019), as stated by the MAH.

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

To assess the immunogenicity of SG or its components, all clinical samples from studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-06, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238, that were available for analysis, were analyzed using the ADA method validated under V1101906E1\\_A1. All ADA confirmed positive clinical samples using the ADA method validated under V1101906E1\\_A1 were analyzed for neutralizing activity using the NAb method validated under RSYP2.

No new information is provided with the current dossier, as there is no change in these bioanalytical methods. The bioanalytical methods to detect the presence of ADAs (V1101906E1\\_A1) and NAbs (RSYP2) will therefore not be further discussed in this report.

## Population PK

## Rationale for developing an integrated PopPK model and context of use

The popPK of SG, free SN-38, and TAb (conjugated and unconjugated anti-Trop-2 antibody), have been previously characterized using the combined concentration-time data from participants with different types of epithelial cancers (study IMMU-132-01), participants with metastatic TNBC (study IMMU-13205), and from participants with HR+/HER2- metastatic breast cancer (mBC) ( study IMMU132-09).

The current analysis applied an integrated model structure with the measured PK data of three analytes: TAb, free SN-38 and total SN-38. In addition to the data included from three clinical studies in the previously developed popPK model, this analysis included additional data from the phase 3 study GS-US-592-6238 (ASCENT-03) in first-line patients with unresectable locally advanced or metastatic TNBC. The PK of SG were now derived based on model-estimated kinetics of conjugated SN-38 and potential change in drug-to-antibody ratio (DAR) over time. In contrast, for the purpose of the previous popPK analysis, SG concentrations were calculated based on an assumed DAR of 8 and the molecular weights for free SN-38 and the loaded hRS7 antibody of 392 Da and 161 kDa, respectively.

Compared to the previous three popPK models (2-compartment models) that were developed separately for each analyte, the integrated model was developed to provide a more mechanistic and flexible structure to describe the dynamic change of TAb and free SN-38 at first cycle and at steady state. Covariate assessment for each analyte was performed during the model development. The PopPK model was also used to identify the effect of intrinsic and extrinsic factors on the exposure to SG, free SN-38, and Tab and to predict individual exposures of SG, TAb and free SN-38 for subsequent exposure-response analyses.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## PK Data Set and Methods

The PopPK analysis dataset included a total of 1063 participants contributing with 8396, 8487, and 8482 observations of total antibody, total SN-38, and free SN-38, respectively, from 4 clinical studies in participants with solid tumours: IMMU-132-01 (phase 1/2), IMMU-132-05 (phase 3), IMMU-132-09 (phase 3), and GS-US-592-6238 (phase 3). The pooled analysis dataset included all participants treated with SG and for whom dosing time and associated concentrations (from at least one post dose visit) were available. For observed Tab, 8260 of 8396 samples were included in the dataset after accounting for inconsistencies, outliers and below limit quantification (BLQ) samples (0.64%). From 8487 observed samples of total SN-38, 7654 were included in the final data set. Most of the excluded observation were classified BLQ (8.5%) and were also excluded prior to model development. For free SN-38, data handling resulted in 8415 samples that were included in the final data set for model development - 5438 quantifiable observations and 2977 BLQ samples (35%). Below the limit of quantification (BLQ) observations were flagged in the popPK analysis dataset and a likelihood-based approach (M3) was implemented.

The popPK analysis was conducted via nonlinear mixed-effects modelling (NONMEM) software, Version 7.5 (ICON Development Solutions, Dublin, UK). Data manipulation, postprocessing, summaries, and plotting were performed using R 4.2 or above.

Population and individual model parameters were estimated using the stochastic approximation expectation maximization (SAEM) method followed by importance sampling Monte Carlo (IMP). The 95% CI of parameter estimates were derived from the covariance matrix of the estimates (NONMEM $COV step).

## Model structure

The structural model was built on prior knowledge from previous modelling and incorporates several assumptions. Conjugated SN-38 and TAb are assumed to share the same PK parameters of clearances and volume of distributions since kinetics are expected to be driven by the monoclonal antibody. Both linear and nonlinear clearance pathways were tested to investigate the necessity of their inclusion in the model. The compartmental model further accounts for the formation kinetics of free SN-38 whose formation kinetics were driven by the deconjugation process - characterized by the deconjugation rate constant (Kdec) - from the conjugated SN-38. The model defined a mass balance such that the sum of free SN-38 and conjugated SN-38 amount corresponded to the observed total SN-38. Both 1compartment and 2-compartment models were assessed for free SN-38 PK, as well as linear and nonlinear elimination pathways.

The concentration of SG (CSG) was calculated as the ratio of conjugated SN-38 concentration to the time-varying drug-antibody ratio (DAR):

<!-- formula-not-decoded -->

<!-- formula-not-decoded -->

TAD represents time after each SG dose. All concentrations are represented in molar units. The DAR at time zero equals 8 and changes with time. As the concentration of SG was the fraction of conjugated SN-38 over DAR, DAR should not take values below 1. A value less than 1 would suggest lack of conjugated SN-38 and the ratio would not be numerically meaningful. Therefore, a minimum DAR of 1

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

## where DAR chänges over time:

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

was assumed to be present for the entire duration of conjugated SN-38 exposure throughout deconjugation.

Figure 2 Integrated model structure

<!-- image -->

Dose of SG is in molar units. CL: linear clearance of TAb and conjugated SN-38, Km: the exposure eliciting half of the maximum effect, Vmax: maximal Michaelis-Menten clearance, Q: intercompartmental clearance of TAb and conjugated SN-38, Vc: central volume of distribution of TAb and conjugated SN-38, Vp: peripheral volume of distribution of TAb and conjugated SN-38, CLf/F: apparent clearance of free SN-38, Qf/F: apparent intercompartmental clearance of free SN-38, Vcf/F: apparent central volume of distribution of free SN-38, Vpf/F: apparent peripheral volume of distribution of free SN-38, Kdec: first order deconjugation rate constant.

## Covariate model and model evaluation

Covariates screened for inclusion into the popPK model were based on mechanistic plausibility, exploratory analysis, and clinical interest. The effects of these covariates on clearance parameters (of both TAb and free SN-38) were included in the full model. The conjugated SN-38 and TAb shared the same PK parameters for clearances and volume of distributions. The covariates, therefore, apply to both analytes. The potential effect of anti-drug antibody (ADA) presence during the SG treatment on clearance was explored.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Table 4 Covariates to assess impact of exposures to total antibody, free, SN-38, and SG

| Factors     | Covariates Included                                                                                                                                                                                |
|-------------|----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Demographic | Sex (male or female), age, race (Asian, White, Black or African American, or other), and body weight.                                                                                              |
| Disease     | Tumor type (TNBC, HR+/HER2– mBC, or other), ECOG (0 or ≥ 1), number of prior cancer treatments (0, 1, 2, 3, 4, or ≥ 5), and baseline tumor size.                                                   |
| Participant | Serum albumin, hepatic impairment based on NCI-ODWG classification (normal, mild, moderate, or missing), renal function or impairment (based on eGFR estimated using MDRD u 10 */9 / 8//1/)  1  () |

ECOG = Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group performance status; eGFR = estimated glomerular filtration rate; HER2– = human epidermal growth factor receptor 2-negative; HR+ = hormone receptor-positive; mBC = metastatic breast cancer; MDRD = Modification of Diet in Renal Disease; NCI-ODWG = National Cancer Institute Organ Dysfunction Working Group; SG = sacituzumab govitecan; TNBC = triple-negative breast cancer; UGT1A1 = uridine diphosphate glucuronosyltransferase 1A1

A full covariate modelling approach emphasizing parameter estimation rather than stepwise hypothesis testing was implemented. The full model was reduced to the final model by removing covariates with 95% CIs of their estimated effects falling within the region of practical equivalence (ROPE), which is commonly defined as 80% to 125% of the null value.

Final model performance was evaluated by visual predictive check (VPC). Post hoc empirical Bayes estimates (EBEs) from the final models were used to calculate exposure metrics (Cmax1, AUC0-168, and Ctrough) of total antibody, free SN-38, and SG. Forest plots were generated with simulations informed by model parameter sets and dataset covariates. A total of 1000 sets of parameters were sampled from distributions based on parameter estimates and the associated variance-covariance matrix of the final model. The influence of each covariate was compared against a reference individual PK parameter. Uncertainty was computed as a 95% CI for each exposure metric.

## Final popPK model and Results

The PK of the TAb and conjugated SN-38 were described by a two-compartment model with linear and nonlinear (Michaelis-Menten [MM]) clearance pathways. Free SN-38 PK were described by a twocompartment model with linear clearance.

Estimates for the effects of age, sex, tumour type, hepatic function, albumin, Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group performance status (ECOG), baseline tumour size, and number of prior lines of therapy in the full covariate model fell within the ROPE for area under the AUC0-168 and Cmax1 of total antibody, free SN-38, and SG. These effects were considered not statistically significant or clinically meaningful and, therefore, not included in the final model. In the final model, the effects of body weight on clearances and volumes were included using allometric scaling with estimated coefficients. The effects of race, renal function, and UGT1A1 genotype were estimated on the clearances on total antibody and free SN-38.

## Impact of Covariates on Exposure

Forest plots depict the impact of the estimated covariate effects on exposure (AUC 0-168 and Cmax1) presenting the ratio of exposures of TAb, free SN-38 and model-derived SG, given a covariate effect, relative to the exposure from a reference subject. The reference range was equivalent to a 20% change on the log scale. The reference subject is a 69 kg White participant with first line advanced or metastatic TNBC, eGFR ≥ 90 mL/min/1.73m2, UGT1A1 genotype of *1/*1, and receiving SG dose of 10 mg/kg.

## Model evaluation

Simulation-based model diagnostics (VPCs) were generated to investigate the predictive performance of the integrated popPK model. Observed data of the three analytes and the model-simulated median, fifth, and 95 th  percentiles for the final model are opposed.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

## ADME

The PK of total antibody (hRS7 unconjugated or conjugated with SN-38), free SN-38, and conjugated SN-38 was characterized in participants with solid tumours using an integrated PopPK model (including data from studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238).

Final model EBEs were used to calculate PK parameters and exposure metrics in participants included in the analysis population and receiving IV SG 10 mg/kg on Days 1 and 8 of 21-day treatment cycles.

## Absorption

Sacituzumab govitecan is administered via IV infusion. No studies characterizing absorption via other routes of administration have been conducted with SG; thus, drug absorption is not applicable. The Tmax of SG occurred at the end of SG infusion across all clinical studies.

## Distribution

Based on the PopPK analyses using data from studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238, the estimated volume of distribution at steady state (Vss) for SG is 4.62 L.

The mean (%CV) of estimated central volume distribution of both total antibody and SG is 2.86 L (19.7%).

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Metabolism

No metabolism studies with sacituzumab govitecan have been conducted. The metabolism of SG is expected to be mediated by both catabolism of hRS7 IgG1κ into small peptides and amino acids in a manner similar to endogenous immunoglobulin (Ig)G. SN-38 (the small molecule moiety of sacituzumab govitecan) is metabolised via UGT1A1.

## Elimination

The median (range) elimination half-life (t1/2) of sacituzumab govitecan and free SN 38, based on population pharmacokinetic analysis was 155 hours (95.8-555) and 21.5 hours (16.0-259), respectively.

The mean (%CV) terminal elimination half-life of SG is 161 hours (23.2%) and the mean (%CV) apparent half-life of free SN-38 is 23.5 hours (50%).

The mean (%CV) of clearance of total antibody and SG is 0.0117 L/hr (29.4%) and 0.132 L/hr (19.8%), respectively.

No excretion studies have been conducted with SG. SN-38 and SN-38G are reported to be primarily excreted through the hepatobiliary route, with lesser amounts detected in the urine.

## Dose proportionality and time dependencies

Final model EBEs were used to calculate PK parameters and exposure metrics in participants included in the analysis population and receiving IV SG 10 mg/kg on Days 1 and 8 of 21-day treatment cycles.

Model-predicted concentration-time courses indicated minimal accumulation of SG and free SN-38, while the accumulation of total antibody was moderate.

## Pharmacokinetics in target population

## Study GS-US-592-6238

Of the 279 participants who were randomized to receive SG in study GS-US-592-6238, PK samples were available from 272 participants.

Serum samples for PK analyses were collected only for participants receiving SG. Collection times for PK samples were predose and after the end of infusion on Day 1 and Day 8 of Cycle 1; Day 8 of Cycles 2, 6, and 10. Thereafter, predose samples were collected on Day 8 of every 8 cycles after Cycle 10 (e.g. Cycle 18 Day 8, Cycle 26 Day8); and at the end of treatment (EOT) visit.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

In study GS-US-592-6238 the mean Cmax for total antibody, total SN-38, and free SN-38 ranged from approximately 226,000 to 342,000 ng/mL, 4470 to 4930 ng/mL, and 85.6 to 129 ng/mL, respectively.

For total SN-38 or free SN-38, mean Cmax appeared to reach steady state approximately by Cycle 2.

For total antibody, Cmax slightly increase over time (up to Cycle 10).

No apparent accumulation over time was observed for total antibody, total SN-38 or free SN-38.

## Special populations

## Effect of Intrinsic Factors

The PopPK analysis was used to evaluate the broader potential impact of demographic and diseaserelated factors on PK as covariates from all 4 studies across various cancer types.

<!-- image -->

## Renal impairment

Mild (n = 464) and moderate (n = 91) renal impairment had no clinically relevant effect on SG, free SN-38, or total antibody exposure compared with participants with normal (n = 506) renal function for the population included in the PopPK analysis. The potential effect of severe (n = 2) renal impairment could not be appropriately estimated due to the low number of participants included in the analysis dataset.

## Hepatic impairment

Mild (n = 317) hepatic impairment had no clinically relevant effect on SG, free SN-38, or total antibody exposure compared with participants with normal (n = 742) hepatic function for the population included in the PopPK analysis. Moderate (n = 4) hepatic impairment also indicated no clinically meaningful effect; however, this assessment should be interpreted with caution as the number of participants included in the dataset are limited.

## Age

Age had no effect on total antibody, free SN-38, or SG exposure for the overall population.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

Median Ratío [95% CI]

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Sex

Sex (male/female) had no effect on total antibody, free SN-38, or SG exposure for the overall population.

## Body Weight

For total antibody, free SN-38, and SG, the model-predicted AUC0-168 for a body weight of 49 kg (5th percentile) and a body weight of 104 kg (95th percentile) were estimated to be 17.7%, 17.5%, and 16% lower and 25%, 26%, and 23% higher for the participants with metastatic TNBC when compared with a typical participant (having body weight of 69 kg) with metastatic TNBC, respectively.

## Race

Race had no effect on SG, free SN-38, or total antibody exposure for the overall population.

## UGT1A1 Genotype

No significant differences in total antibody, free SN-38, or SG exposure were observed in participants with the UGT1A1*28/*28 (n = 112) or UGT1A1*1/*28 (n = 410) genotype compared with participants with the UGT1A1*1/*1 (n = 413). Due to low frequency of occurrence for UGT1A1*1/*6 (n = 13) and UGT1A1*6/*6 (n = 2) alleles, these genotypes were combined with all other genotypes. There was a potential impact of these genotypes on SN-38 exposures; however, given the low sample size these conclusions should be treated with caution.

## Tumor Type

No significant differences in total antibody, SN-38, or SG exposure were observed by tumour type.

## Pharmacokinetic interaction studies

## Effect of Extrinsic Factors

No drug-drug interaction studies have been conducted with SG.

Concomitant administration of SG with UGT1A1 inhibitors may increase the incidence of adverse reactions due to the potential increase in systemic exposure to SN-38. Exposure to SN-38 may be reduced in participants concomitantly receiving UGT1A1 enzyme inducers.

Among the 1063 participants assessed in the PopPK analyses, only a few participants received either UGT1A1 inhibitors (N = 15) or inducers (N = 7) during SG treatment.

## 2.3.3. Pharmacodynamics

## Mechanism of action

Sacituzumab govitecan (SG) is a trophoblast cell-surface antigen-2 (Trop-2)-directed antibody-drug conjugate (ADC) consisting of a humanized anti-Trop-2 monoclonal antibody (hRS7) conjugated with the active metabolite of irinotecan (SN-38) by a hydrolysable linker (CL2A). SG binds to Trop 2expressing tumour cells and is internalised with the subsequent release of SN 38 from a hydrolysable linker. SN 38 interacts with topoisomerase I and prevents re ligation of topoisomerase I induced single strand breaks. The resulting DNA damage leads to apoptosis and cell death.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Primary and secondary pharmacology

## Immunogenicity

## Study GS-US-592-6238

In study GS-US-592-6238, collection times for immunogenicity (ADA) samples were at predose on Day 1 (Cycle 1); Day 8 (Cycles 2, 6, and 10); and predose on Day 8 of every 8 cycles after Cycle 10 (e.g. Cycle 18 Day 8, Cycle 26 Day 8); at the EOT visit.

The immunogenicity samples for ADA prevalence and incidence assessments were evaluable for 264 and 247 participants, respectively. Of the participants evaluated for ADA prevalence, 1 participant (0.4%) had ADAs to SG at baseline. Of the participants evaluated for ADA incidence, 3 participants (1.2%) had treatment-emergent ADAs to SG. All 3 participants with treatment-emergent ADAs were classified as having persistent ADA responses. No participant had treatment-boosted ADAs.

The maximum reportable ADA titer for participants with ADA-positive samples was 90.

All 3 participants who had treatment-emergent persistent ADAs also had positive NAb assessments.

## Integrated summary of immunogenicity across studies

An overall summary and cross-study comparison of ADA responses to SG in participants who received at least 1 dose of SG 10 mg/kg are presented the table below. Immunogenicity samples for ADA prevalence and incidence assessments were evaluable for 1157 and 1058 participants, respectively, across studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-06 (Cohorts 1 and 2), IMMU-132-09, and GSUS-592-6238.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

15 of 1157 participants evaluable for ADA prevalence (1.3%) had positive-ADA results. Among these, 2 participants (0.2%) were ADA positive only at baseline and 13 participants (1.1%) had positive postbaseline ADA results.

13 of 1058 participants evaluable for ADA incidence (1.2%) had treatment-emergent ADAs to SG. 12 participants (1.1%) were classified as having persistent ADA responses and 1 participant (&lt; 0.1%) was classified as having a transient ADA response to SG. Among participants with treatment-emergent ADAs, the onset of ADAs was observed at their last visit (10 of 13 participants; range: 22 to 245 days after first SG dose for participants with onset at the last visit).

The maximum reportable ADA titer observed across the studies ranged from 10 to 90.

No participant had treatment-boosted ADAs.

Ten of the 13 participants with treatment-emergent ADAs also had positive NAb assessments.

- a Persistent ADA: treatment-induced ADA at ≥ 2 samples during the treatment (with ≥ 16 weeks between first and last positive) or treatment-induced ADA in the last sample or with &lt; 16 weeks before an ADA-negative last sample.

à ADA incidence (treatment-emergent ADA): the sum of both treatment-induced and treatment-boosted ADA.

b Transient ADA: treatment-induced ADA that does not meet the definition of persistent ADA.

- d NAb incidence: proportion of participants with ≥ 1 positive NAb result based on the total N evaluable for ADÅ incidence as denominator.
- C Treatment-Boosted ADA: positive baseline and ([max titer of the postbaseline ADA] / [titer of baseline ADA]) ≥ 9.

## Impact of Antidrug Antibodies on Sacituzumab Govitecan or Total Antibody Pharmacokinetics

The impact of immunogenicity on the PK of free SN-38, total SN-38, and total antibody was evaluated in the population PK (PopPK) analysis based on available serum concentration and ADA data in the PopPK analysis population from studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-5926238.

Of the 13 participants with treatment-emergent ADAs, PK data were available for 7 participants (n = 4 from study IMMU-132-05; n = 3 from study GS-US-592-6238). In addition, PK data were also available for 1 participant with baseline positive ADAs from study GS-US-592-6238 that was included in the PopPK analysis dataset.

## Impact of Antidrug Antibodies on Efficacy

Across the studies, 5 participants who were ADA positive had a stable disease, 2 participants had progression disease and one participant had a partial response. 3 participants were not assessed/not available for best overall response assessment and for two participants the best overall response was not evaluable per independent review assessment. The progression-free survival in ADA positive patients ranged from 1.1 to 5.0 months and the overall survival ranged from 1.41 to 20.3 months.

Due to the small number of participants with positive ADA responses to SG across studies IMMU-13201, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-06, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238, no formal analysis was performed by the applicant to assess the impact of ADAs on the efficacy of SG.

## Impact of Antidrug Antibodies on Safety

An evaluation of immunogenicity and safety for participants with treatment-emergent ADAs to SG has been evaluated in studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-06, and GS-US-592-6238.

All 13 of 1058 participants (1.2% incidence) with treatment-emergent ADAs received a starting dose of SG 10 mg/kg. None of these participants experienced a serious treatment-emergent AE (TEAE) that was considered related to SG.

Participant-level ADA status: \"ADA+\" if the participant has treatment-emergent ADA; \"ADA-\" if the participant is evaluable for ADA incidence and does not have treatment-emergent ADA; missing if the participant is not evaluable for ADA incidence.

A participant with ≥ 2 AEs in each row is counted only once. A participant may be counted in multiple categories.

Adverse events were coded per MedDRA Version 27.1. Severitv grades were defined per CTCAE Version 5.0.

Adverse events leading to dose reduction were not collected in Study MMU-132-01; study participants were excluded in pooled percentage calculations.

One of the 13 participants (7.7%) with treatment-emergent ADAs experienced a TEAE that led to premature discontinuation of study drug. The TEAE was in the AESI hypersensitivity category (a Grade 2 infusion-related reaction that resolved the same day) and did not recur upon receiving an additional dose of SG. This participant also had a positive NAb assessment.

No participant had treatment-emergent immune-mediated AEs.

## 2.3.4. PK/PD modelling

## Exposure-Response Relationships

Using an integrated population pharmacokinetic (popPK) model that characterized 1) total SN-38, 2) free SN-38, and 3) total SG antibody (tAb) concentrations following SG administration, exposureresponse (E-R) analyses were conducted to characterize the relationships between exposure and efficacy and safety endpoints of clinical interest. Individual empirical Bayes estimates (EBE) of PK parameters from this popPK model were used to calculate the exposure metrics of tAb, SG and free SN-38, which were tested in the presented E-R analyses. In total, up to 26 metrices were considered for E-R analyses regarding efficacy and 12 additional metrices (for SN38) for E-R analyses regarding safety.

Exposure-response (E-R) for efficacy analyses were conducted using data from a total of 272 participants with metastatic TNBC from study GS-US-592-6238, and exposure-safety analyses were conducted using data from a total of 1063 participants with solid tumours who received SG in studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238.

## Exposure-response (E-R) analysis for efficacy

Exposure-efficacy relationships were evaluated in participants with locally advanced unresectable or metastatic TNBC who received a starting dose of SG 10 mg/kg on Days 1 and 8 of a 21-day cycle in study GS-US-592-6238. The exposure-efficacy analysis dataset included a total of 272 participants

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

with locally advanced unresectable or metastatic TNBC from study GS-US-592-6238 who had estimated exposure metrics based on PopPK model and data for respective efficacy endpoints.

The evaluated efficacy endpoints included PFS and ORR.

The exposure-efficacy relationships were analyzed using binomial logistic regression models for ORR and parametric time-to-event (TTE) models for PFS.

## · Exposure-PFS

The exposure-efficacy relationships were analyzed using parametric time-to-event (TTE) models for PFS (N=272). For PFS, Cmin,SS,SG was identified as the most significant exposure metric and implemented as an Emax drug effect on the baseline hazard.

## Exposure-response (E-R) analysis for safety

Exposure-safety relationships were evaluated in participants with various advanced epithelial cancers or advanced or metastatic breast cancers who received a starting dose of SG 8 mg/kg (16 participants from studies IMMU-132-01 and IMMU-132-05), 10 mg/kg (1044 participants from studies IMMU-13201, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238), or 12 mg/kg (3 participants from study IMMU-132-01) on Days 1 and 8 of a 21-day cycle.

The exposure-safety analysis dataset included a total of 1063 participants (98.2% in the SG 10-mg/kg starting dose group) from studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238 who had PopPK parameter estimates to enable estimation of exposure metrics related to SG dosing and had data for the respective safety endpoints.

Rare events (&lt; 5%) of the selected AEs were not analyzed in the exposure-safety analysis. For the following safety endpoints, a parametric logistic regression model was used to assess the relationship between SG exposure and safety outcome, as well as explore known prognostic factors (covariates): adverse event of special interest (AESI) neutropenia (any grade/Grade 3 or higher), neutropenia only (preferred term [PT] = neutropenia; any grade/Grade 3 or higher), febrile neutropenia (any grade/Grade 3 or higher), infections (any grade/Grade 3 or higher), vomiting (any grade), diarrhoea (any grade/Grade 3 or higher), AESI hypersensitivity (any grade), and nausea (any grade).

In addition, a semiparametric Cox proportional hazards model was used to assess the relationship for time to AEs leading to dose reductions and time to AEs leading to dose delays versus SG exposure, as well as explore prognostic factors (covariates).

A statistically significant relationship between Cmax, D1,SG and any grade/grade 3 or higher neutropenia, febrile neutropenia and diarrhoea has been observed. A statistically significant relationship between Cmax, D1,SG and any grade nausea has been observed.

No statistically significant relationship was observed between SG exposure and any grade or Grade 3 or higher infections and infestations, vomiting. No statistically significant relationship was observed between SG exposure and any grade hypersensitivity. A statistically significant relationship between Cmax, D1,SG and the time to AEs leading to dose reduction has been observed.

## 2.3.5. Discussion on clinical pharmacology

The clinical pharmacology package of sacituzumab govitecan so far comprised study GS-US-592-6238 and three completed clinical studies (study IMMU-132-01, study IMMU-132-05, and study IMMU-13209) contributing to the characterization of PK and immunogenicity of SG, and one ongoing study (study IMMU-132-06) contributed data to the immunogenicity package as well.

In the pivotal study GS-US-592-6238 for the current application for extension of the indication of sacituzumab govitecan (SG, Trodelvy), the recommended dose of SG is 10 mg/kg administered intravenously (IV) once weekly on Days 1 and 8 of continuous 21-day treatment cycles until disease progression or unacceptable toxicity.

The pharmacokinetics of SG for the proposed dosing regimen of 10 mg/kg administered intravenously (IV) once weekly on Days 1 and 8 of continuous 21-day treatment cycles had already been characterized in previous applications (e.g. initial MAA application in TNBC).

In the pivotal study GS-US-592-6238, sparse PK sampling was collected. The PK of total antibody, SG and free SN-38 was characterized in participants with solid tumours using an integrated PopPK model. The integrated PopPK model was also used to evaluate the effect of various intrinsic and extrinsic factors on the exposure of total antibody, SG, and free SN-38. Data from studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU 132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238 were used to develop the model.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Bioanalytical methods

The bioanalytical methods submitted for the determination of total SN-38, free SN-38/SN-38G and total antibody (hRS7-IgG and HRS7-SN38) in human serum, were found overall acceptable for their intended purpose.

## Pharmacokinetics

In the pivotal study GS-US-592-6238 pre-(Ctrough) and post-dose (Cmax) concentrations were collected. The mean Cmax for total antibody, total SN-38, and free SN-38 ranged from approximately 226,000 to 342,000 ng/mL, 4470 to 4930 ng/mL, and 85.6 to 129 ng/mL, respectively and were similar compared to the concentrations reported in previous studies.

The data from studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238 were used to develop an integrated PopPK model to characterize the PK of total antibody, free SN-38, and conjugated SN-38 in participants with solid tumours.

The absorption, distribution, metabolism, and excretion of SG, total antibody and free SN-38, total SN38, SN-38G, was well-characterised and described in the initial TNBC application and have been updated based on the results of the integrated PopPK model.

## Integrated popPK model

A population PK analysis was conducted based on data from studies GS-US-592-6238, IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, to characterize the disposition of Sacituzumab Govitecan. PK of total antibody, and conjugated and free SN-38, were described by a two-compartment model for each of the species, with linear clearance for free SN-38 and linear and nonlinear clearance for total antibody and conjugated SN-38. Of note, all studies showed a very pronounced percentage of BLQ samples for free SN-38. Data handling resulted in 8415 samples that were included in the final data set for model development - 5438 quantifiable observations and 2977 BLQ samples (35%). These BLQ observations were flagged in the popPK analysis dataset and a likelihood-based approach (M3) was implemented and is agreed. The current population analysis applied an integrated model structure with the measured PK data of three analytes: TAb, free SN-38 and total SN-38 including additional data from the phase 3 study GS-US-592-6238 (ASCENT-03) in first-line patients with unresectable locally advanced or metastatic TNBC. Previous model-based description of these analytes were based on separate popPK models. Along with this change in model structure, two strong assumptions regarding the PK of SG have been considered. First, the PK of SG were now derived based on model-estimated kinetics of conjugated SN-38 and potential change in drug-to-antibody ratio (DAR) over time. In contrast, for the purpose of the previous popPK analysis, SG concentrations were calculated based on an assumed DAR of 8 and the molecular weights for free SN-38 and the loaded hRS7 antibody of 392 Da and 161 kDa, respectively. Second, conjugated SN-38 and TAb are assumed to share the same PK parameters of clearances and volume of distributions since kinetics are expected to be driven by the monoclonal antibody. Both assumptions are deemed overall plausible, however they impact the concentration of SG, that is solely based on model-based simulations, with no confirmatory data available. The MAH provided a comparison of former and current predictions of SG PK and the cSGtime-course. The provided justifications for changes in t1/2 and AUC as well as for the implementation of DAR (which was shown to be the main driver in the mention exposure metrics) are deemed reasonable.

## PopPK model parameters and model performance

The integrated model is characterized by several covariates on PK parameters for each of the analytes that were observed to be correlated which is expected also due to the integrated new structure.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

One pivotal parameter Kdec could be estimated acceptably well, however, covariate selection and inter-individual variability (IIV) parameters (10 parameters in total), that show moderate to high shrinkage (up to 78.3% for Km) with partially fixed variance parameters indicate some model deficiencies. Allometric scaling factors were estimated on CL,Q and Vc,Vp to 0.428 and 0.523 are below the expected ones for a monoclonal antibody. This may be attributed to interference with the other covariates that were identified statistically relevant and on the assumed lumping of tab and cSN38 PK behaviour.

Body weight is the most influential covariate on the PK of the total antibody, Free SN-38, and SG AUC and Cmax1, almost exceeding the reference range at both the lower (49 kg) and higher (104 kg) body weight range. This became relevant for conducted exposure-response-analyses, also showing the trends of gain of benefit but also increase in safety endpoint with exposure. In addition, UGT1A1 genotype is indicated to have a potentially clinically relevant effect on Free SN-38 exposure (AUC and Cmax1), which is discussed in the exposure-response analyses section.

Prediction-corrected VPC of free SN-38 indicated a slight underprediction of p95 later than 150 hrs after dose and slight overprediction in the period before. Pronounced BLQ percentage after 150 hrs after dose (data and simulations) are observed. The pcVPCs of tab and total SN-38 are deemed acceptable. A slight underprediction of the median tab up to 10000 hrs after first dose could be identified. VPCs of total antibody at 10 mg/kg stratified by study indicate no consistent trends, however, prediction-corrected VPC of total antibody vs time after dose indicated underprediction of median and p5. VPC of total (free and conjugated) SN-38 at 10 mg/kg by study indicate well performance for the previously included studies, whereas for the clinical study relevant for this indication, the model has issues in describing the first 100 hrs after dose. The same trend is indicated for free SN-38 at 10 mg/kg, that might also interfere with the slight under-prediction of free SN-38 BLQ percentage in this study.

The model-derived exposure (mean Cmax and mean AUC of SG and free SN-38) during cycle 1 was higher in the integrated popPK model compared to the serum pharmacokinetics of sacituzumab govitecan and SN-38 evaluated in the ASCENT study (population of mTNBC patients who received sacituzumab govitecan as a single agent at a dose of 10 mg/kg body weight) and previously reported in the SmPC. Especially AUC is more than twice as high for SG. In addition, the predicted half-life for SG was higher than previously reported. The reasons for these differences, the quite high predicted AUC(0-168h) and t1/2 for SG, needed to be further clarified by the MAH. In this context, a comparison between the previous pop-PK model and the current pop-PK model for all three analytes and a summary table with the descriptive PK parameters: mean Cmax, mean Ctrough, and mean AUC(0-168h) for the four different studies, which are included in the integrated pop-PK model (studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238), and for the three analytes (total antibody, total SN-38, and free SN-38) were provided by the MAH and in general showed reasonable similarity.

Section 5.2 of the SmPC has been updated based on the results of the integrated PopPK-model.

## Immunogenicity

In  study  GS-US-592-6238 ,  the  immunogenicity  samples  for  ADA  incidence  assessments  were evaluable for 247 participants. 3 of these participants (1.2%) had treatment-emergent ADAs to SG. All 3 participants with treatment-emergent ADAs were classified as having persistent ADA responses and were also NAb positive. The incidence of ADA to SG was low in study GS-US-592-6238 and was similar to the immunogenicity results previously reported for SG.

Across studies , immunogenicity samples for ADA prevalence and incidence assessments were evaluable for 1157 and 1058 participants, respectively, across studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-132-06 (Cohorts 1 and 2), IMMU-132-09, and GS-US-592-6238.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

The currently presented data indicates a low prevalence and incidence of ADA across the studied patient populations. The incidence of treatment-emergent ADA to SG was low (N=13 [1.2%]). Neutralizing antibodies were rare (N=10 [0.9%]). The maximum reportable ADA titer observed across the studies ranged from 10 to 90.

However, a potential trend has been observed, that the ADA status might have an impact on the exposure of free SN-38, SG and total antibody. Due to the low occurrence of ADAs, the impact of positive ADAs on the PK is therefore currently uncertain.

Based on the individual study efficacy results presented, no clear impact of ADA on efficacy was identified, whereas analyses of progression-free survival, overall survival, and objective response rate presented by study and ADA status showed a numerically higher efficacy in the ADA- group when compared with the ADA+ group across studies. However, the prevalence of participants who were ADA+ ( ≤ 5 participants who were ADA+ in each study) is low and the results should therefore be interpreted with caution. Nevertheless, a trend has been observed and thus a potential impact on the efficacy can not currently be excluded.

Moreover, no clear impact of ADAs on safety have been identified at present. The occurrence of any TEAE appears similar between participants with or without ADAs to SG across individual studies and pooled populations. However, in the pooled all treated SG population, the incidence (≥10% difference) of the following treatment-emergent AEs: TEAE with Grade 3 or higher, serious TEAE, and all deaths, were higher in participants who were tested positive for ADAs compared to participants tested negative for ADAs. Such differences in the occurrence of treatment-emergent AEs between ADA positive and ADA negative participants was especially observed in study GS-US-592-6238 SG (10 mg/kg). Nevertheless, it needs to be considered that the number of participants who were tested positive for ADAs was very low in study GS-US-592-62 (N=3) and in the pooled all treated SG population (N=13). Therefore, the results should be interpreted with caution.

Overall , the currently limited data of ADA-positive patients available limits the ability to conclusively determine whether positive ADAs have an impact on pharmacokinetics, efficacy, and safety. Therefore, no final conclusion can be drawn at present and the impact of positive ADAs on the PK, efficacy and safety of SG is currently unknown and needs to be further evaluated during the ongoing clinical studies and the clinical development of SG.

## Exposure-response analyses

Exposure-response analyses were conducted to evaluate the relationships between SG-related exposure and its efficacy endpoints (as described by PFS and ORR) and safety endpoints (as described by AESI Neutropenia, Neutropenia Only, Febrile Neutropenia, Infections and Infestations, Vomiting, Diarrhea, Hypersensitivity, Nausea, AEs leading to dose reductions, AEs leading to dose interruptions). Exposures of tAb, SG and free SN-38 increased with increasing body weight under body weight-based dosing. The effect of body weight was statistically significant. Individual empirical Bayes estimates (EBE) of PK parameters from this popPK model were used to calculate the exposure metrics of tAb, SG and free SN-38, which were tested in the presented E-R analyses.

## Exposure-Efficacy-Relationship

Exposure-response (E-R) for efficacy analyses were conducted using data from a total of 272 participants with metastatic TNBC from study GS-US-592-6238.

The evaluated efficacy endpoints included PFS and ORR and the exposure-response relationships were analyzed using binomial logistic regression models for ORR and parametric time-to-event (TTE) models for PFS. Investigated PK metrices are indicated to be highly correlated.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

Kaplan-Meier plot for PFS stratified by popPK predicted Cmin,SS,SG quartiles revealed statistically significant relationships between Cmin,SS,SG and PFS. The median survival times across quartiles of Cmin,SS,SG showed that Cmin,SS,SG levels in Q1 are associated with a higher risk of PFS events and that higher exposure (higher exposure quartiles) is associated with longer median survival times.

In addition to Cmin,SS,SG, baseline albumin was identified as a statistically significant predictor of PFS. The Kaplan-Meier plot for PFS stratified by popPK predicted baseline albumin quartiles showed that baseline albumin levels in Q1 are associated with a higher risk of disease progression or death (lower risks of PFS events) whereas baseline albumin levels greater than Q1 are associated with lower risk of disease progression or death (lower risks of PFS events). However, there was no clear trend within quartiles 3 and 4 of baseline albumin patients. It was noted that although the final PFS TTE model only picked albumin as the significant predictor, other factors, especially those unbalanced and disease related ones between Q1 and Q2-4 may still have had some effect and contributed to the PFS difference. In addition, exposure-efficacy analyses are limited since exposure is only based on one dose level.

Using a logistic regression model , statistically significant relationships were identified between Cmin,SS,SG and independent ORR and PK exposure metrics within the range of SG dose of 10 mg/kg. For every 25% increase in Cmin,SS,SG, the odds are 1.29-fold higher.

Overall, the exposure-response analyses for efficacy demonstrated that a PFS and ORR benefit of SG appears to be dependent on exposure, with increasing benefit with increase in exposure. There were imbalances in patient characteristics across the quartiles of exposure. As also suggested by popPK, Q1 patients had lower body weight, and also higher baseline tumour size, higher lactate dehydrogenase (LDH) and more patients with mild hepatic impairment.

## Exposure-Safety-Relationship

Exposure-response (E-R) for safety analyses were conducted using data from a total of 1063 participants with solid tumours who received SG in studies IMMU-132-01, IMMU-132-05, IMMU-13209, and GS-US-592-6238. Individual SG, free SN-38 and total antibody exposure metrics for the participants in the analysis population were derived based on a population PK model for these studies.

Using a logistic regression model, statistically significant E-R relationships between Cmax,D1,SG and AESI Neutropenia, Neutropenia Only, Febrile Neutropenia and Diarrhoea were identified.

In addition, statistically significant E-R relationships were identified between Cmin,C1,SG and Any Grade Nausea.

Kaplan-Meier estimates of Cmax,D1,SG quartiles and Time to AEs Leading to Dose Reductions showed a ER-relationships between Cmax,D1,SG and Time to AEs leading to dose reductions. The probability of AEs leading to dose reduction increased with higher quartiles (increasing exposure).

In general, a higher risk (odds ratio &gt;1) of associated neutropenia related AEs and non-neutropenia related AEs as diarrhoea and Time to AEs leading to dose reductions was identified for every 25% increase in Cmax,D1,SG.

Overall, the exposure-response analyses with regards to safety indicated also a dependency on exposure with higher probability of event or Odds Ratio with increase in exposure (Cmax SG).

Moreover, a higher risk (odds ratio &gt;1) of associated Grade 3 or higher AESI Neutropenia, Grade 3 or higher Neutropenia Only and Any Grade Febrile Neutropenia as well as time to AEs leading to dose reductions was identified for the UGT1A1 genotype *1/*28 and *28/*28 in comparison to *1/*1 genotype evaluated. This is also indicated in the popPK model (forest plots).

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

However, special warnings and precautions for use in patients with reduced UGT1A1 activity and information regarding interaction with UGT1A1 inhibitors and UGT1A1 inducers are already included in section 4.4, 4.5 and 4.8 of the SmPC.

Special warnings and precautions for use regarding the ADRs neutropenia and diarrhoea are also included in sections 4.2 and 4.4. of the SmPC.

## 2.3.6. Conclusions on clinical pharmacology

In general, pharmacokinetics and pharmacodynamics of sacituzumab govitecan have been sufficiently characterized. Results from the pivotal study GS-US-592-6238, supporting this application for extension of indication, appear overall consistent with the analyses provided in previous applications.

## 2.4. Clinical efficacy

## 2.4.1. Dose response study

The dosing regimen of SG in study ASCENT-03 (10 mg/kg IV D1 and D8, Q3W) is the same as already approved for the treatment of patients with unresectable or metastatic TNBC and HR+, HER2- breast cancer after at least two prior systemic therapies. The SG dose of 10 mg/kg was selected based on results from study IMMU-132-01, a phase 1/2 dose escalation and expansion phase study in metastatic epithelial cancers.

## 2.4.2. Main study

ASCENT-03 (GS-US-592-6238): A randomized, open-label, phase 3 study of sacituzumab govitecan versus treatment of physician's choice in patients with previously untreated, locally advanced, inoperable or metastatic triple-negative breast cancer whose tumours do not express PD-L1 or in patients previously treated with anti-PD-(L)1 agents in the early setting whose tumours do express PD-L1

## Figure 20 ASCENT-03 Study Schema

<!-- image -->

## Stratification Factors:

- De novo versus recurrent disease within 6-12 months from completion of treatment in the curative setting versus recurrent disease occurring &gt; 12 months from completion of treatment in the curative setting
- Geographic region (US/Canada/Western Europe versus Rest of World)
