Primary Endpoint: PFS by BICR

Key Secondary Endpoints: OS, ORR by BICR, PROs

Other Secondary Endpoints: DOR, TTR, and safety

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

1L = first-line treatment; BICR = blinded independent central review; chemo = chemotherapy; CPS = combined positive score; DOR = duration of response; mTNBC = metastatic triple-negative breast cancer; ORR = objective response rate; OS = overall survival; PD-L1 = programmed death ligand 1; PFS = progression-free survival; PRO = patient-reported outcome; SG = sacituzumab govitecan; TNBC = triple-negative breast cancer; TPC = treatment of physician's choice; TTR = time to response; US = United States

## Methods

Participants who were randomized to the control group (TPC chemotherapy) were eligible to receive SG through the study in the crossover phase upon disease progression verified by BICR and upon meeting eligibility criteria.

Tumour assessments were obtained by computed tomography (CT) or magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) scans every 6 weeks for the first year, then every 12 weeks thereafter.

All participants were followed for survival until death, loss to follow-up, or withdrawal of consent,

whichever occurred first.

## Study participants

## Main inclusion criteria:

- 1) 18 years of age or older, able to understand and give written informed consent.
- 2) Patients with locally advanced, inoperable, or metastatic TNBC who have not received previous systemic therapy for advanced disease and whose tumors are PD-L1 negative at screening. Alternatively, patients whose tumours are PD-L1 positive at screening will be eligible if they received an anti-programmed death (ligand) 1 (anti-PD-[L]1) agent (i.e. checkpoint inhibitor) in the adjuvant or neoadjuvant setting or if they cannot be treated with an anti-PD-(L)1 agent due to a comorbidity.
- a) Patients must have completed treatment for stage IIII breast cancer, if indicated, and ≥ 6 months must have elapsed between completion of treatment with curative intent (e.g. date of primary breast cancer surgery or date of last (neo)adjuvant chemotherapy administration [including anti-PD-(L)1 treatment], whichever occurred last) and first documented local or distant disease recurrence. Dates of postoperative radiotherapy are not included in this calculation.
- i) Patients who received taxane, gemcitabine, or platinum agents in the (neo)adjuvant setting can be treated with same class of chemotherapy (taxane or gemcitabine/carboplatin) if ≥ 12 months have elapsed between the completion of treatment with curative intent (e.g. date of primary breast tumour surgery or date of last (neo)adjuvant chemotherapy administration, whichever occurred last) and first documented local or distant disease recurrence. ( Note : included with protocol amendment 1)
5. ii) Patients enrolled should have received prior anthracycline in the (neo)adjuvant setting or be considered not eligible for anthracyclines as assessed by the treating physician. ( Note : included with protocol amendment 1 ).
- b) Patients presenting with de novo metastatic TNBC are eligible for this study. Note : They were capped at approximately 35% of all enrolled participants.
- c) specimen.
8. TNBC status and tumour PD-L1 CPS will be confirmed centrally on a recent or archival tumor Patients must have histologically or cytologically documented TNBC, according to current
9. ASCO/CAP criteria, defined as negative for ER, progesterone receptor, and HER2 (Allison et al.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

2020, Wolff et al. 2018). Patients initially diagnosed with hormone receptor-positive or HER2positive breast cancer must have central confirmation of TNBC in a tumour biopsy obtained from a local recurrence or distant metastasis prior to entry. Tumour combined positive score (CPS) &lt; 10 using the PD-L1 IHC 22C3 assay will be required for eligibility. Alternatively, patients with tumou r CPS ≥ 10 will be eligible if they received an anti -PD-(L)1 agent (i.e. checkpoint inhibitor) in the adjuvant or neoadjuvant setting or if they cannot be treated with an anti-PD-(L)1 agent due to a comorbidity.

- d) Patients must have measurable disease by CT or MRI as per RECIST Version 1.1 criteria as evaluated locally. Tumour lesions situated in a previously irradiated area are considered measurable if unequivocal progression has been documented in such lesions since radiation.
- 3) Have provided representative formalin-fixed paraffin-embedded (FFPE) tumour specimen in blocks (preferred) or have at least 20 to 25 freshly sectioned unstained slides from fresh biopsy tissue (preferred) or archival tissue block for central testing of ER, progesterone receptor, HER2, and PDL1 and additional biomarker testing.
- 4) ECOG performance status score of 0 or 1.
- 5) Life expectancy ≥ 3 months.
- 6) Recovered from major surgery for ≥ 2 weeks.
- 7) Adequate hematologic counts without transfusional or growth factor support within 2 weeks of study treatment initiation (hemoglobin ≥ 9 g/dL, ANC ≥ 1500/mm3, and platelets ≥ 100,000/μ L).
- 8) Adequate hepatic function (bilirubin ≤ 1.5 x ULN, AST and ALT ≤ 2.5 x ULN or ≤ 5 x ULN if known liver metastases, and serum albumin &gt; 3 g/dL).
- 9) Creatinine clearance ≥ 30 mL/min as assessed by the Cockcroft -Gault equation.
- 10) International Normalized Ratio (INR)/PT and PTT or aPTT ≤ 1.5 ULN unless patient is currently receiving therapeutic anticoagulant therapy.
- 11) Male patients and female patients of childbearing potential who engage in heterosexual intercourse must agree to use protocol-specified method(s) of contraception.
- 12) Patients with HIV must be on antiretroviral therapy (ART) and have a well-controlled HIV infection/disease.

## Main exclusion criteria:

- Patients may not have received systemic anticancer treatment (with the exception of endocrine therapy) within the previous 6 months or radiation therapy within 2 weeks prior to enrolment. Patients must have recovered (i.e. &gt; Grade 2 is considered not recovered) from AEs due to a previously administered agent at the time of study entry.
- Have previously received topoisomerase 1 inhibitors or antibody drug conjugates containing a topoisomerase inhibitor.
- Have known active central nervous system (CNS) metastases and/or carcinomatous meningitis. Patients with previously treated brain metastases may participate (with the exception of those treated with chemotherapy) provided they have stable CNS disease (defined as radiographic stability demonstrated with a minimum of 2 posttreatment brain imaging assessments; one performed during screening) for at least 4 weeks prior to enrolment and all neurologic symptoms have returned to baseline, have no evidence of new or enlarging brain metastases, and have also

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

been clinically stable for at least 2 weeks while taking ≤ 10 mg/day of prednisone or its equivalent. All patients with carcinomatous meningitis are excluded regardless of clinical stability.

- Met any of the following criteria for cardiac disease:
- a) Myocardial infarction or unstable angina pectoris within 6 months of enrolment.
- b) History of serious ventricular arrhythmia, high-grade atrioventricular block, or other cardiac arrhythmias requiring antiarrhythmic medications (except for atrial fibrillation that is well controlled with antiarrhythmic medication); history of QT interval prolongation.
- c) New York Heart Association Class III or greater congestive heart failure or known left ventricular ejection fraction of &lt; 40%.
- Have active chronic inflammatory bowel disease (ulcerative colitis, Crohn's disease) or GI perforation within 6 months of enrollment.
- Have active serious infection requiring antibiotics.
- Have active HBV or HCV
- Has received a live vaccine within 30 days prior to randomization.

## Treatments

Sacituzumab govitecan (SG): 10 mg/kg intravenously (IV) on Days 1 and 8 of 21-day cycles.

The treatment of physician's choice chemotherapy ( TPC ) was selected prior to randomization from 1 of the 3 allowed regimens:

- Paclitaxel 90 mg/m 2  IV on Days 1, 8, and 15 of 28-day cycles; or
- nab-Paclitaxel 100 mg/m 2  IV on Days 1, 8, and 15 of 28-day cycles; or
- Gemcitabine 1000 mg/m 2  IV plus carboplatin AUC 2 IV on Days 1 and 8 of 21-day cycles.

## Duration of treatment

Participants received study drug until blinded independent central review (BICR)-verified disease progression, unacceptable toxicity, withdrawal of consent, initiation of other anticancer therapy (including any investigational agent), or death.

Treatment beyond BICR -verified disease progression per Response Evaluation Criteria in Solid Tumours Version 1.1 (RECIST v1.1) was permitted if there was evidence of clinical benefit per the investigator and the patient was tolerating the study drug, if agreed upon by the investigator and the sponsor medical monitor.

No estimands were defined.

## Sample size

Approximately 540 patients were planned to be randomised in a 1:1 ratio to receive either SG or TPC over a planned non-uniform accrual period of 20 months.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

The primary analysis of PFS was planned to be conducted when approximately 352 PFS events as assessed by BICR have occurred. With 352 events, the study provided more than 95% power to demonstrate superiority in PFS of SG relative to TPC at a 1-sided alpha of 2.5%, assuming proportional hazards with a true HR of 0.65, median PFS time for the TPC arm of 5.6 months, and a 30% annual dropout rate. The target number of events was expected to occur approximately 27.6 months after the first patient was randomised.

For the final analysis of the secondary endpoint OS, 391 events were needed to detect an average HR of 0.75 with 80% power at a 1-sided significance level of 2.5% using a log-rank test, given 2 efficacy interim analyses at 70% and 85% information fraction, respectively. Assuming a median OS time for the TPC arm of 17.5 months, with a total sample size of 540 patients, and a 5% annual dropout rate, it was estimated that the final OS analysis would occur at approximately 56 months after the first patient was randomised.

## Randomisation

Randomisation occurred centrally using an interactive voice response system/integrated web response system (IWRS). Patients were randomised in a 1:1 ratio to SG or physician's choice of chemotherapy starting on Day 1.

Randomisation was stratified by:

- -De novo versus recurrent disease within 6 to 12 months from completion of treatment in the curative setting versus recurrent disease occurring &gt; 12 months from completion of treatment in the curative setting.
- -Geographic region (US/Canada/Western Europe versus rest of the world).

Curative treatment interval was defined as systemic (neo)adjuvant breast cancer therapy or surgery (whichever occurred last) and first local or distant recurrence. Adjuvant radiotherapy was not included in the 6-month interval.

## Blinding (masking)

This was an open-label study. The investigators and patients were not blinded to treatment assignment. For the sponsor study management team, until the in-house study unblinding, the access to the treatment assignment was limited and controlled, depending on the functional or study roles. The details of the controlled access setup were described in a data access restriction plan (DAP).

According to the DAP, restricted members of the Gilead Study Management Team (Clinical Development and Study Biostatistician) were not permitted to aggregate efficacy data by assigned treatment group until study unblinding at the time of data finalization for the PFS primary analysis. Additionally, no aggregated analysis with treatment-related information for primary or key secondary efficacy endpoints or efficacy surrogate endpoints by assigned treatment group was allowed until data finalization for the PFS primary analysis, except for safety monitoring purposes (e.g. for the Data Monitoring Committee [DMC] or Patient Safety to monitor safety signals).

Tumour response was measured by an independent centralised and blinded group of radiology experts who assessed tumour response using RECIST version 1.1 criteria.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Statistical methods

## Analysis Population

ITT analysis set: The ITT analysis set included all randomised patients according to the treatment arm to which the patient was randomised to. The ITT Analysis set was the primary analysis set for efficacy analyses, demographic characteristics, baseline assessments, and quality of life assessments.

Safety analysis set: The safety analysis set included all patients who received at least 1 dose of any study treatment, with treatment assignments designated according to the actual treatment received. This analysis set was the primary analysis set for all safety analyses.

PK analysis set: The PK analysis set included all randomised patients who received at least 1 dose of SG per the protocol and had at least 1 measurable post treatment serum concentration of SG.

Immunogenicity analysis set: The Immunogenicity analysis set included all randomised patients who received at least 1 dose of SG and had at least 1 evaluable non missing anti-SG antibody test result.

## Efficacy Analysis

## PFS assessed by BICR

PFS was defined as the time from the date of randomisation until the date of first documentation of objective progressive disease, as assessed by BICR per RECIST Version 1.1, or death from any cause (whichever comes first). The primary analysis of PFS comparing SG versus TPC was performed using the log-rank test stratified by randomisation factors in the ITT analysis set. The hazard ratio with the corresponding 2-sided 95% CIs estimated using a Cox proportional hazard regression model stratified by randomisation stratification factors were planned. PFS was planned to be summarised by treatment arm using Kaplan-Meier estimates, including median and the proportion of event-free patients at benchmark time points such as 3, 6, 12 and 18 months. Kaplan-Meier plots were planned to be provided.

The following sensitivity analyses were planned:

- -PFS assessed by investigator
- -PFS using different censoring rules.

Censoring rules for the primary and sensitivity analyses are provided in the below table.

## OS

OS was defined as the time from the date of randomisation until death due to any cause. For participants who were not known to have died at the time of the analysis, OS data was censored at the last date that they were known to be alive. In the event that the participant was lost to follow-up or withdrew consent from the study, the survival status may have been obtained from publicly available resources under applicable local laws.

The analysis of OS was planned to be performed using a similar methodology as for the primary analysis of PFS.

To account for the effect of crossover on OS, methods such as the rank preserving structural failure time model, two-stage method, or inverse probability censoring weighting method were planned.

## ORR assessed by BICR

ORR was defined as the proportion of participants who achieved complete response or partial response that was confirmed at least 4 weeks after initial documentation of response as assessed by BICR per RECIST Version 1.1. Tumour response assessments after the date of participants receiving new anticancer therapy were excluded from the analysis. Participants, who did not have sufficient baseline or on-study tumour status information that was not adequate for response status assessment or received new anticancer therapy prior to achieving CR or PR, were considered as non-responders.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

ORR assessed by BICR was planned to be analysed and compared between treatment arms in the ITT analysis set using the Cochran Mantel-Haenszel test stratified by the stratification factors used in the randomisation. The 2-sided 95% CIs for each treatment arm was planned to be calculated using the Clopper-Pearson exact method.

The following sensitivity analyses were planned:

- -ORR assessed by investigator.

Concordance/discordance of best overall response as assessed by BICR and investigator was planned to be summarised in a frequency table.

## Quality of Life Analysis

Mean change from baseline in physical functioning domain as measured by EORTC QLQ-C30 was planned to be analysed using linear mixed model for repeated measures (MMRM) longitudinal analysis based on the ITT analysis set.

The time to deterioration (TTD) of fatigue domain of the EORTC QLQ-C30, measured as the time between the date of randomisation and the date of assessment at which a patient experienced a deterioration (i.e. ≥ 10 points worsening from baseline in the fatigue domain) or death, was planned to be assessed using the Kaplan-Meier method for the ITT analysis set. The TTD distribution of the two treatment arms was planned to be compared using the log-rank test, stratified by the randomisation stratification factors. The hazard ratio with the corresponding 2-sided 95% CIs estimated using a Cox proportional hazard regression model stratified by randomisation stratification factors were planned.

## Other secondary endpoints

DOR assessed by BICR and investigator were planned to be analysed using Kaplan-Meier methodology including estimates of median and 95% CIs.

Time to response (TTR) assessed by BICR and investigator were planned to be summarised using descriptive statistics by treatment arm for responders.

## Multiplicity

The overall type I error rate for this study was controlled at a 1-sided alpha of 2.5%.

The primary endpoint analysis of PFS assessed by BICR served as the gatekeeper for the secondary endpoint analyses: OS, ORR and analysis for QoL (TTD in fatigue and change from baseline in physical functioning), which were planned to be tested sequentially when the above hypotheses in the hierarchy were statistically significant. For OS, the 1-sided alpha of 0.0005% was used to account for the descriptive noncomparative analysis at the time of PFS analysis, and 1-sided alpha of 2.495% for the comparative analysis in the formal test. If both, PFS and OS were tested significantly, 1-sided alpha of 2.5% was used to test ORR and QoL endpoints.

The QoL endpoints TTD in fatigue and change from baseline in physical functioning at Week 25 were planned to be tested when the above endpoints in the hierarchy were all statistically significant. The total 1-sided alpha of 2.5% was split between the 2 tests evenly, initially. If the test of TTD in fatigue was significant at a 1-sided alpha of 1.23%, then this 1-sided alpha were to be passed to the test of change from baseline in physical functioning at Week 25 resulting in a 1-sided alpha of 2.5%. Similarly, if the test of change from baseline in physical functioning at Week 25 was significant at a 1sided alpha of 1.25%, then TTD in fatigue was tested at a 1-sided alpha of 2.5%.

The ORR and QoL were planned to be analysed and tested in the same dataset that is used for OS analysis.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

## Interim Analyses

The study planned for 3 interim analyses (IA) and 1 final analysis.

At the first analysis, which was the primary analysis for PFS, PFS was planned to be tested when approximately 352 PFS events would have occurred using a 1-sided alpha level of 2.5% after approximately 27.6 months after the first patient was randomised. At the same time, a descriptive, noncomparative analysis of OS was planned to be performed using a 1-sided alpha of 0.005% without formal hypothesis testing. It was expected to observe 218 OS events (56% information fraction of the total 391 OS events) at IA1.

At the second analysis, which was the first interim analysis for OS (IA1), OS was planned to be tested when approximately 274 (70% information fraction) deaths would have been observed at approximately 34 months after the first patient was randomised.

At the third analysis, which was the second interim analysis for OS (IA2), OS was planned to be tested when approximately 332 (85% information fraction) deaths would have been observed at approximately 43 months after the first patient was randomised.

At the final analysis, OS was planned to be tested when approximately 391 deaths would have been observed at approximately 56 months after the first patient was randomised.

The first analysis was planned to serve as the final analysis for PFS. No interim analysis of PFS was planned.

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

To account for the interim analyses of OS, a nominal 1-sided alpha of 0.005% was spent at the first analysis for a noncomparative and descriptive analysis of OS, while the Lan-DeMets alpha spending function that approximates an O'Brien Fleming approach was used to adjust the remaining alpha of 2.495% for IA1, IA2 for OS and the final analysis, resulting in nominal alpha of 0.74%, 1.28% and 2.01% at IA2, IA3 and the final analysis, respectively.

Details on the expected number of events and 1-sided alpha levels at analysis are provided in the table below.

Table 23 Expected number of events at interim and final analyses

| Description                                                          | Expected Events n (Information Fraction)   |   Expected Timing of Analysis (Months From Randomization) | Stopping Boundary (1-Šided Alpha)                    |
|----------------------------------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------------------------------|

## Treatment in the control arm

Among 276 participants in the TPC group who received study treatment, 55.8% (154 participants) received a taxane (paclitaxel or nab-paclitaxel) and 44.2% (122 participants) received gemcitabine with carboplatin).

## Subsequent treatment

Of the 196 participants in the TPC group who received second line anticancer therapy, 154 participants (55.2%) received SG. Of these, 125 received SG through the crossover phase of the study, and the remainder received commercial SG in the second-line setting.

## Duration of follow-up

At the time of the primary PFS analysis (DCO 02 April 2025), the median duration of OS follow-up was 13.31 months (range: 0.07, 29.21) in the SG group and 13.14 months (range: 0.03, 27.86) in the TPC group; total: 13.2 (0.03 to 29.21) months.

At the time of OS IA1 (DCO 27 October 2025), the median duration of OS follow-up was 17.74 (0.07 to 36.04) months in the SG group and 17.64 (0.03 to 34.69) months in the TPC group; total: 17.72 (0.03 to 36.04) months.

## Recruitment

The first participant was randomized on 27 October 2022 (on 20 July 2022 the first patient was screened) and the last participant was enrolled on 29 July 2024. The trial is ongoing; 02 April 2025 was the data cut-off date (DCO) for the primary PFS analysis, 27 October 2025 was the DCO for OS IA1.

Participants were enrolled in 229 study centres across 30 countries:

- Africa (n=13): South Africa 13
- Asia Pacific (n=140): Australia 11, China 17, Hong Kong 3, Japan 43, Malaysia 18, South Korea 37, Taiwan 11
- Europe (n=219): Austria 4, Belgium 7, Czech Republic 9, Israel 16, France 22, Germany 15, Hungary 8, Italy 36, NL 6, Poland 8, Romania 10, Slovakia 3, Spain 39, Switzerland 1, Turkey 31, UK 4
- Latin America (n=142): Argentina 22, Brazil 52, Chile 27, Mexico 41
- North America (n=44): Canada 9, US 35.

## Conduct of the study

## Protocol amendments

Original protocol dated 27 October 2021

Excerpt from statistical considerations:

The primary analysis of the PFS primary end point as assessed by BICR was to be conducted in the ITT Analysis Set when approximately 227 PFS events have occurred across the treatment arms and will be

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

tested at the 1-sided significance level of 2.5%. The primary analysis was projected to occur at approximately 20 months after the first patient is randomized.

OS analyses: A descriptive, noncomparative analysis of OS was to be performed at the time of the PFS final analysis. To be conservative, a nominal 1-sided alpha of 0.005% will be spent even without formal hypothesis testing. The descriptive OS summary was to include Kaplan-Meier estimates of median OS by treatment arms and hazard ratio between treatment arms. It is estimated that 114 OS events (~29% information fraction of the total 391 OS events) will occur at this time of analysis.

The study planned to have 2 interim efficacy analyses of the secondary end point, OS, performed when approximately a total of 254 (65% information fraction) and 332 (85% information) death events have occurred, respectively. The interim analyses were projected to occur approximately 32 months and 44 months after the first patient is randomized, respectively.

The final analysis of the key secondary end point of OS was to be conducted in the ITT Analysis Set when approximately 391 death events occurred across the treatment arms (391/540 events with 72% maturity), which was projected to occur at approximately 57 months after the first patient was randomized.

Amendment 1 dated 31 January 2022 (before randomisation of first patient)

The primary reason for this amendment was to address the feedback received from the CHMP regarding study GS-US-592-6238 (EMA SA November 2021), see summary of main changes:

- 'Time to deterioration of global health status/quality of life (QOL), pain, and fatigue' replaced with 'Mean change from baseline in the physical functioning'.
- Stratification by geographic region updated from 'US/Canada vs rest of world' to 'US/Canada/Western Europe vs rest of world' to more accurately reflect the different treatment practices and outcomes between different regions and the contributions of each region to the study plan.
- Updated inclusion criterion 2) to add that patients who received taxane, gemcitabine, or platinum agents in the (neo)adjuvant setting can be treated with same class of chemotherapy if ≥ 12 months have elapsed between the completion of treatment with curative intent and disease recurrence.
- Updated inclusion criterion 2) to add that patients enrolled should have received prior anthracycline in the (neo)adjuvant setting or be considered not eligible for anthracyclines as assessed by the treating physician.
- Update of the primary analysis: PFS analysis will be conducted in the first 400 randomized patients (PFS Analysis Set) instead of the ITT population in order to increase the data maturity and followup time at the time of PFS analysis. The primary analysis will be conducted when approximately 227 PFS events have occurred across the treatment arms in the PFS Analysis Set; it is projected to occur at approximately 22 months after the first patient is randomized, which is about 6 months after the last patient in the PFS Analysis Set is randomized. This analysis of the primary end point will serve as the final analysis for this end point.
- Added sensitivity analyses for PFS based on different censoring rules.

Amendment 2 dated 30 August 2023 (189 participants have been randomised)

Summary of main changes:

- The primary end point analysis was revised, including:
- o Changed the number of PFS events (from 227 to 280)

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

- o Changed from PFS Analysis Set to ITT Analysis Set

To follow the ITT principle, the primary PFS analysis was to be performed in the ITT analysis set. The number of PFS events was updated to 280 in order to achieve 95% power at a 1-sided significance level of 2.5% using a log-rank test.

- The number of OS events in the descriptive summary at the time of PFS analysis was revised. Descriptive summary of OS will be provided at the time of primary PFS analysis in the ITT analysis set. The corresponding number of OS events at the time of PFS analysis in the ITT Analysis Set was updated accordingly.
- Specified the Week 25 timepoint for physical functioning domain of the EORTC QLQ-C30 in the secondary end points.
- Added comparison of time to deterioration (TTD) in fatigue as measured by the EORTC QLQ-C30 between the 2 arms.
- Inclusion criteria were revised to include:
- o Patients with tumour CPS ≥ 10 or PD-L1 positive at screening will be eligible if they cannot receive treatment with an anti-PD-(L)1 agent due to a comorbidity.

Patients with PD-L1 positive mTNBC who have comorbidities precluding treatment with anti-PD(L)1 agents have limited treatment options. The amended criterion allows for patients with mTNBC who are not eligible to be treated with anti-PD-(L)1 agents in the first-line metastatic setting to be enrolled.

- The de novo cap for the mTNBC population was changed from 25% to 35%, and clarification was added for consistency with the Study Design Overview.

Thirty-five percent de novo representation is more reflective of recent real-world data reports.

- Language has been added for instances of treatment beyond the initial BICR-assessed PD per RECIST Version 1.1 to allow patients to continue receiving treatment if there is evidence of clinical benefit.
- Added bone scan when clinically indicated as a new study procedure.

Amendment 3 dated 14 May 2024 (499 out of 558 participants have been randomised)

## Key changes:

- The primary end point analysis was revised, including:
- o Changed the number of PFS events (from 280 to 352)
- The first OS interim analysis timing has correspondingly been adjusted

Rationale for change: Based on the study design in protocol amendment 2 (30 August 2023), 280 progression-free survival (PFS) events were required for the planned PFS primary analysis, corresponding to limited data maturity of 52% with respect to the total population, and only 2.4 months of follow-up after the last patient is enrolled. Based on the assumed median PFS in both arms and given that this is the only and final PFS analysis, a significant number of patients may still be on treatment at the time of the PFS primary analysis with inadequate follow-up time to observe PFS events. In this protocol amendment, the data maturity rate has been increased to 65% (352 of 540 events) to ensure that the PFS analysis is not planned too early and allows for adequate follow-up to observe PFS events in the fully enrolled population, consistent with health authority advice. The first overall survival (OS) interim analysis timing has correspondingly been adjusted to ensure sufficient time between the PFS primary analysis and the first OS interim

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

analysis. The text was also clarified to explain the scenarios in which PFS and OS may be performed at the same time.

- Revised to perform patient-reported outcomes (PRO) analysis on the Intent-to-Treat (ITT) Analysis Set, consistent with health authority advice.
- Text added to clarify that when complete response (CR) is achieved, a bone scan is only required if bone lesions were present at baseline.

## Amendment 4 dated 18 November 2024 (last patient enrolled 29 July 2024)

## Rationale for key changes:

- Strengthen the guidance on the use of G-CSF for the management of neutropenia (in line with SG investigator brochure (IB) update to Edition 14, dated 22 October 2024, and EU EMEA/H/C/005182/II/0037 variation application, dated 24 October 2024, to revise the product information to include updated G-CSF primary prophylaxis mitigation language).
- o Fatal infections in the setting of neutropenia have been observed in clinical trials with TRODELVY, primarily in the first two cycles of treatment.
- o Primary prophylaxis with G-CSF is recommended starting in the first cycle of treatment in patients at increased risk of febrile neutropenia, e.g. older patients (in particular aged 65 years and older), patients with previous neutropenia, poor performance status, organ dysfunction (including renal, liver or cardiovascular dysfunction), or multiple comorbid conditions. Monitor absolute neutrophil count during treatment.
- o Dose modification may be required due to neutropenia or febrile neutropenia. Treat neutropenia with G-CSF and consider prophylaxis in subsequent cycles as clinically indicated.
- o Risk factors for febrile neutropenia per the American Society of Clinical Oncology were included to identify patients who may benefit from primary prophylaxis with granulocyte colony-stimulating factor
- Addition of statement in section 8 that details of any deviations from the original statistical analysis planned will be provided in the SAP

Statistical Analysis Plan Version 1.0 dated 01 April 2025 (all patients randomized)

The SAP Version 1.0 is based on the Protocol Amendment 4 dated 18 November 2024 and was finalized after all patients have been randomized, one day prior to data cut-off for the PFS primary analysis.

To account for the effect of crossover on OS, methods such as the rank preserving structural failure time model, two-stage method, or inverse probability censoring weighting method were planned but not provided yet.

## Protocol deviations

An important protocol deviation was defined as a protocol deviation that might significantly impact completeness, accuracy, and/or reliability of study data or that may significantly affect a participant's rights, safety, or well-being.

Table 27 Important Protocol Deviations (ITT) - DCO 02 April 2025

|                                                           | SG (N = 279)   | TPC (N = 279)   | Total (N = 558)   |
|-----------------------------------------------------------|----------------|-----------------|-------------------|
| Participants with at least 1 Important Protocol Deviation | 150 (53.8%)    | 106 (38.0%)     | 256 (45.9%)       |
| Other treatment compliance issue                          | 89 (31.9%)     | 26 (9.3%)       | 115 (20.6%)       |
| Eligibility criteria                                      | 33 (11.8%)     | 33 (11.8%)      | 66 (11.8%)        |
| Missing data                                              | 39 (14.0%)     | 26 (9.3%)       | 65 (11.6%)        |
| Informed consent                                          | 26 (9.3%)      | 20 (7.2%)       | 46 (8.2%)         |
| Other                                                     | 18 (6.5%)      | 19 (6.8%)       | 37 (6.6%)         |
| Off schedule procedure                                    | 15 (5.4%)      | 12 (4.3%)       | 27 (4.8%)         |
| Wrong treatment or incorrect dose                         | 6 (2.2%)       | 4 (1.4%)        | 10 (1.8%)         |

Further clarifications regarding reported categories of important protocol deviations (IPD):

## · Other Treatment Compliance Issue

'Other Treatment Compliance Issues' were reported with higher incidence in the SG group (31.9%) versus the TPC group (9.3%). In the SG group, this was primarily due to nonobservance to the absolute neutrophil count requirements as outlined in the protocol (N=51 with SG, N=0 with TPC), and additional training was conducted by the sponsor. These cases predominantly included SG administration at Grade 2 ANC levels prior to Day 1 dosing across various cycles. The second largest

\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_\\_

<div style=\"page-break-after: always\"></div>

subcategory contributing to this imbalance was related to faster infusion time than specified per protocol or instances where infusion times were not recorded (N=28 with SG, N=2 with TPC).

## · Eligibility criteria

The study was analyzed using intent to treat principles, and no participants were excluded even if they were subsequently found to have not met eligibility criteria, provided it was deemed safe to continue by the treating Investigator.

## · Missing Data

The IPDs categorized as 'Missing Data' were associated with laboratory and tumour assessments that were not performed during the study or were conducted outside the protocol specified assessment window. IPDs did not result in censoring of PFS.

## · Informed Consent

Important protocol deviations regarding informed consent primarily involved administrative errors. There were no instances in which informed consent was not obtained from a participant in the clinical study.

## · Other

Occurrence of important deviations in the 'Other' category were primarily due to stratification errors and delayed reporting of SAEs.

## · Off Schedule Procedure

Deviations were related to tumour assessments completed outside of the protocol prespecified window. IPDs did not result in PFS censoring.

## · Wrong Treatment or Incorrect Dose

Deviations were related to the dosing errors of study treatment. The majority of these dosing errors were due to the dose not being recalculated after patient body weight changes. No participants received the wrong study treatment.

## Numbers analysed

Table 32 Numbers in analysis populations

|                              | SG           | TPC          | Total        |
|------------------------------|--------------|--------------|--------------|
| Screened                     |              |              | 887          |
| ITT Analysis Set             | 279 (100.0%) | 279 (100.0%) | 558 (100.0%) |
| Safety Analysis Set          | 275 (98.6%)  | 276 (98.9%)  | 551 (98.7%)  |
| Pharmacokinetic Analysis Set | 272 (97.5%)  | 0            | 272 (48.7%)  |
| Immunogenicity Analysis Set  | 264 (94.6%)  | 0            | 264 (47.3%)  |

Screened Population: Participants who have signed an informed consent and participated in the screening procedures at site to assess eligibility.

Intent-to-treat (ITT) Analysis Set includes all participants who were randomized in the study.

Safety Analysis Set includes randomized participants who have received at least one dose of any study drug.

Pharmacokinetic Analysis Set includes randomized participants who received ≥ 1 SG dose and have ≥ 1 measurable posttreatment SG concentration.

Immunogenicity Analysis Set includes randomized participants who received ≥ 1 SG dose and have ≥ 1 evaluable non-missing

anti-SG antibody test result.

The denominator of percentages is the number of participants in each treatment group in the ITT Analysis Set.

| No PD and No Death with New Anticancer Therapy                                   | 26 (9.3%)            | 22 (7.9%)            |
| No Baseline or Postbaseline Evaluable Assessment a                               | 6 (2.2%)             | 6 (2.2%)             |
| Kaplan-Meier Estimate of PFS (Months) (95% CI) b                                 |                      |                      |
| Median                                                                           | 9.69 (8.15, 11.14)   | 6.93 (5.62, 8.25)    |
| Kaplan-Meier Estimate of PFS Rate (95% CI) c                                     |                      |                      |
| At 3 Months                                                                      | 0.851 (0.802, 0.889) | 0.786 (0.732, 0.831) |
| At 6 Months                                                                      | 0.652 (0.590, 0.708) | 0.532 (0.469, 0.592) |
| At 9 Months                                                                      | 0.519 (0.454, 0.580) | 0.352 (0.291, 0.414) |
| At 12 Months                                                                     | 0.409 (0.343, 0.474) | 0.243 (0.186, 0.304) |
| At 18 Months                                                                     | 0.261 (0.191, 0.336) | 0.127 (0.071, 0.201) |
| Stratified Log-rank P value of SG vs TPC d                                       | < 0.0001             | -                    |
| Stratified Hazard Ratio of SG vs TPC (95% CI) from Cox Model d                   | 0.623 (0.501, 0.775) | 0.623 (0.501, 0.775) |

CI = confidence interval; ITT = intent to treat; IWRS = interactive web response system; PD = progressive disease; PFS = progression-free survival; Q1 = first quartile; Q3 = third quartile; RECIST v1.1 = Response Evaluation Criteria in Solid Tumors Version 1.1; SG = sacituzumab govitecan; TPC = treatment of physician's choice

a Censoring due to no baseline or no postbaseline evaluable assessment does not include death event before the 2nd scheduled visit postbaseline.

a PFS (months) = (date of events or censoring - date of randomization + 1)/30.4375. The 95% CI is based on log-log transformation.

b PFS rate is the proportion of participants alive without PD.

c The 2-sided P value is from stratified log-rank test and the hazard ratio with 95% CIs calculated using Cox proportional hazards model, adjusted for randomization stratification factors (IWRS).

## Secondary Efficacy Endpoints

At the time of the PFS primary analysis (DCO 02 April 2025), descriptive analyses are provided for the key secondary endpoints of OS, ORR, mean change from baseline in the physical functioning domain of the EORTC QLQ-C30 at Week 25, and median TTD in the fatigue domain of the EORTC QLQ C30. Additional secondary endpoints included DOR and TTR.

Analysis uses an MMRM including data from all visits up to and including Week 25.

## Time to Deterioration (TTD) of fatigue domain of the EORTC QLQ C30

Deterioration was defined as a ≥ 10 points worsening from baseline in the fatigue domain.

Median TTD in the fatigue domain of the EORTC QLQ-C30 was 1.45 (95% CI: 1.08, 1.68) months in the SG and 1.64 (95% CI: 1.18, 1.94) months in the TPC groups (HR: 0.979; 95% CI: 0.803, 1.193).

Figure 28 KM Plot of TTD of Fatigue Domain of the EORTC QLQ C30 (ITT) (DCO 02 April 2025)

<!-- image -->

TTD is defined as the time in months (30.4375 days) between randomization date and the date of assessment at which a participant experienced a deterioration (≥ 10 points worsening from baseline in the fatigue domain) or death.

The two-sided P value is from stratified log-rank test and the HR with 95% CIs are calculated using Cox proportional hazards model, adjusted for randomization stratification factors collected in IWRS

## Efficacy by BRCA central testing at OS IA1

An exploratory objective of the study as per the protocol was to conduct tumour whole exome sequencing (WES) analyses in a central laboratory. These analyses included participants with sufficient formalin-fixed paraffin-embedded (FFPE) tumour material for the WES-based BRCA assessment and the correlation of BRCA1/BRCA2 mutation status with efficacy endpoints. The Biomarker Analysis Set (BAS) comprised 423 participants (SG, n = 217 and TPC, n = 206), of which 18.2% had a BRCA1/2 mutation.

Figure 32 Forest Plot of PFS by BICR Across BRCA 1 and 2 Subgroups (BAS) - DCO 27 October 2025

<!-- image -->

BRCA1/2 status was derived from whole-exome sequencing using tumor samples.

Survival time estimated with Kaplan-Meier method. Confidence Interval for median computed using the Brookmeyer-Crowley method.

Hazard ratio and CI are derived from an unstratified Cox regression analysis, with treatment as the only predictor.

## Efficacy by Trop-2 expression (exploratory analysis)

Evaluation of baseline trophoblast cell-surface antigen 2 (Trop-2) expression in fresh or archival tumour tissue as a biomarker for efficacy was an exploratory endpoint. Trop-2 expression in tumour tissue was assessed by immunohistochemistry (IHC) using a fit-for-purpose, validated EPR20043 formulation locked assay (FLA) at Roche Tissue Diagnostics (RTD). Trop-2 data were available from 499 participants (89.4%) in the Intent to Treat (ITT) Analysis Set = Biomarker Analysis Set (BAS).

## Sensitivity analyses of overall survival

At the time of OS IA1, a total of 154 participants (55.2%) in the TPC group received SG in the secondline setting; 125 of these 154 participants received SG during the crossover phase of the study and the remainder received commercial SG in the second-line setting.

To adjust for the effect of crossover on OS, prespecified sensitivity analyses using 3 simplified 2-stage model [TSE], inverse probability of censoring weighting [IPCW], and rank preserving structural failure time model [RPSFT]) were performed, in which the crossover to SG by participants in the TPC group per protocol was considered ( n = 125 ).

Using the TSE method, 139 (49.8%) and 82 (29.4%) participants in the SG and TPC groups had OS events after re-censoring survival times for participants in the TPC group and the adjusted OS HR (95% CI) of SG versus TPC was 0.622 (0.442, 0.859).

Using the IPCW method, 139 (49.8%) and 81 (29.0%) participants in the SG and TPC groups had OS events after censoring crossover participants in the TPC group. The adjusted OS HR (95% CI) of SG versus TPC was 0.727 (0.518, 1.048).

Using the RPSFT method, 139 (49.8%) and 141 (50.5%) participants in the SG and TPC groups had OS events after re-censoring survival times for participants in the TPC. The adjusted OS HR (95% CI) of SG versus TPC was 0.908 (0.723, 1.133).

In addition, exploratory analyses were performed to adjust for the treatment switch to second line SG in the TPC group (including participants in the TPC group who received SG provided by the study in the crossover phase and also those who received SG through commercial means in the second line [ n = 154 ]) which resulted in similar HR point estimates.

## Exploratory Efficacy Analyses

Progression-Free Survival on Next-Line Therapy ( PFS2 ) at OS IA1

PFS2 was defined as the time from randomization to the first documented progression on next-line therapy per investigator assessment or death due to any cause, whichever occurred first.

## Table 46 PFS2 at OS IA1- DCO 27 October 2025

|                                                               | SG (N = 279)         | TPC (N = 279)        |
|---------------------------------------------------------------|----------------------|----------------------|
| Number (%) of Participants with Events                        | 172 (61.6%)          | 190 (68.1%)          |
| Disease Progression (PD)                                      | 86 (30.8%)           | 129 (46.2%)          |
| Death                                                         | 86 (30.8%)           | 61 (21.9%)           |
| Number (%) of Participants Censored                           | 107 (38.4%)          | 89 (31.9%)           |
| Kaplan-Meier Estimate of PFS2 (Months) (95% CI) a             |                      |                      |
| Median                                                        | 16.16 (14.82, 19.58) | 13.83 (12.48, 15.84) |
| Kaplan-Meier Estimate of PFS2 Rate (95% CI)b                  |                      |                      |
| At 3 Months                                                   | 0.971 (0.943, 0.986) | 0.967 (0.938, 0.983) |
| At 6 Months                                                   | 0.859 (0.812, 0.895) | 0.869 (0.823, 0.903) |
| At 9 Months                                                   | 0.764 (0.709, 0.810) | 0.762 (0.706, 0.808) |
| At 12 Months                                                  | 0.658 (0.598, 0.710) | 0.586 (0.525, 0.642) |
| At 18 Months                                                  | 0.466 (0.405, 0.525) | 0.378 (0.319, 0.437) |
| Stratified Log-rank p-value of SG vs TPCc                     | 0.0181               |                      |
| Stratified Hazard Ratio of SG vs TPC (95% CI) from Cox Modelc | 0.778 (0.632, 0.958) |                      |

PFS2 is defined as the time from date of randomization to the first documented progression on next-line therapy based on investigator assessment of PD or death due to any cause, whichever occurs first. Next-line therapy is defined as the first new systemic anticancer therapy (including crossover treatment) initiated after discontinuation of study treatment regardless of end of treatment reason.

a Quantile of PFS2 is from Kaplan-Meier estimate. The 95% CI is based on log-log transformation.

b PFS2 rate is the proportion of participants alive without PD at the next line of therapy.

c The two-sided P value is from stratified log-rank test and the hazard ratio with 95% CIs are calculated using Cox proportional hazards model, adjusted for randomization stratification factors from interactive web response system (IWRS).

| Design                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Study GS-US-592-6238 is an ongoing international, multicenter, open-label, randomized, Phase 3 study designed to compare the efficacy and safety of SG versus TPC in participants with locally advanced unresectable or metastatic triple-negative breast cancer (TNBC) who have not received previous systemic therapy for advanced disease and who are not candidates for programmed cell death protein 1 (PD-1) or programmed cell death ligand 1 (PD-L1) inhibitors. This study enrolled participants with tumors that are PD-L1 negative (defined as having a tumor combined positive score [CPS] < 10 using the PD-L1 immunohistochemistry [IHC] 22C3 pharmDx assay), and participants with tumors that are PD-L1 positive (defined as having a CPS ≥ 10) if they previously received a PD -1 or PD-L1 inhibitor in the neoadjuvant/adjuvant setting or have a comorbidity precluding treatment with a PD-1 or PD-L1 inhibitor. Participants presenting with de novo metastatic TNBC were eligible for this study and were capped at approximately 35% of all enrolled participants. Approximately 540 eligible participants were planned to be randomized in a 1:1 ratio to receive 1 of the following 2 treatments: • SG: 10 mg/kg intravenously (IV) on Days 1 and 8 of 21-day cycles • TPC: 21- or 28-day cycles The TPC was selected prior to randomization from 1 of the 3 allowed regimens: 1) paclitaxel 90 mg/m2 IV on Days 1, 8, and 15 of 28-day cycles; 2) nanoparticle albumin-bound (nab)-paclitaxel 100 mg/m2 IV on Days 1, 8, and 15 of 28-day cycles; or 3) gemcitabine 1000 mg/m2 IV with carboplatin area under the curve (AUC) 2 IV on Days 1 and 8 of 21-day cycles. Randomization was stratified by the following factors: • De novo versus recurrent disease within 6 to 12 months from completion of treatment in the curative setting versus recurrent disease occurring > 12 months from completion of treatment in the curative setting. • Treatment-free interval was defined as the time between completion of systemic | Study GS-US-592-6238 is an ongoing international, multicenter, open-label, randomized, Phase 3 study designed to compare the efficacy and safety of SG versus TPC in participants with locally advanced unresectable or metastatic triple-negative breast cancer (TNBC) who have not received previous systemic therapy for advanced disease and who are not candidates for programmed cell death protein 1 (PD-1) or programmed cell death ligand 1 (PD-L1) inhibitors. This study enrolled participants with tumors that are PD-L1 negative (defined as having a tumor combined positive score [CPS] < 10 using the PD-L1 immunohistochemistry [IHC] 22C3 pharmDx assay), and participants with tumors that are PD-L1 positive (defined as having a CPS ≥ 10) if they previously received a PD -1 or PD-L1 inhibitor in the neoadjuvant/adjuvant setting or have a comorbidity precluding treatment with a PD-1 or PD-L1 inhibitor. Participants presenting with de novo metastatic TNBC were eligible for this study and were capped at approximately 35% of all enrolled participants. Approximately 540 eligible participants were planned to be randomized in a 1:1 ratio to receive 1 of the following 2 treatments: • SG: 10 mg/kg intravenously (IV) on Days 1 and 8 of 21-day cycles • TPC: 21- or 28-day cycles The TPC was selected prior to randomization from 1 of the 3 allowed regimens: 1) paclitaxel 90 mg/m2 IV on Days 1, 8, and 15 of 28-day cycles; 2) nanoparticle albumin-bound (nab)-paclitaxel 100 mg/m2 IV on Days 1, 8, and 15 of 28-day cycles; or 3) gemcitabine 1000 mg/m2 IV with carboplatin area under the curve (AUC) 2 IV on Days 1 and 8 of 21-day cycles. Randomization was stratified by the following factors: • De novo versus recurrent disease within 6 to 12 months from completion of treatment in the curative setting versus recurrent disease occurring > 12 months from completion of treatment in the curative setting. • Treatment-free interval was defined as the time between completion of systemic |

| Secondary endpoint   | Objective response rate (ORR)                                                                           | Defined as the proportion of participants who achieve a complete response (CR) or partial response (PR) that is confirmed at least 4 weeks after initial documentation of response as assessed by BICR per RECIST v1.1.                                                                                                                                  |
| Secondary endpoint   | Duration of response (DOR)                                                                              | Defined as the time from the first documentation of CR or PR to the earlier of the first documentation of definitive PD or death from any cause (whichever comes first) as assessed by BICR per RECIST v1.1.                                                                                                                                             |

TTD of fatigue domain of the EORTC QLQ-C30 is defined as the time between the date of randomization and the date of assessment at which a participant experienced a deterioration (ie, ≥ 10 points worsening from baseline in the fatigue domain) or death |
